Retraction of Li'an and Remarriage: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on retraction and remarriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a husband who retracts his li'an can remarry his wife, identify the proofs on both sides, and state the tarjih position.

Core Idea
Retraction ends the li'an state, so the hadith's 'never' applies only during li'an.

After li'an and judicial separation, if the husband retracts his accusation, he becomes liable for hadd al-qadhf. But can he remarry his former wife? The two imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say yes, while Abu Yusuf and others hold a permanent prohibition. This lesson dissects their proofs and the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
After li'an, the judge separates the couple. If the husband later admits he lied (retracts), he is punished with hadd. The question: can he remarry her?
The retraction is not a simple apology; it incurs a legal penalty.
2
State the Hanafi position of the two
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the retraction voids the li'an ruling, so remarriage is permissible.
They treat the hadith as conditional on the state of li'an.
3
State the opposing position
Abu Yusuf, Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and al-Shafi'i say the hadith establishes permanent prohibition (hurmat mu'abbadah).
The same hadith is read as absolute.
4
Follow the opposing proof
Imam Abu Yusuf cites the hadith: 'al-mutala'inani la yajtami'ani abadan' (the two who perform li'an will never be together). He takes 'abadan' as absolute.
This is a dalil naqli from a hadith.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response
The two interpret 'as long as they are engaged in li'an'; after retraction, neither the li'an nor its ruling remains, so the prohibition ends. Also, retraction makes the husband liable for hadd, forfeiting his eligibility for li'an.
The Hanafi response uses taqyid (restriction) of the 'illa (state of li'an).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اللعان
۱۴۸
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پشیم ہے اور نہیں جمع ہوں گے جب تک وہ دونوں لعان کرنے والے ہیں اور اپنے آپ کو بہلانے کے بعد نہ لعان باقی رہا اور نہ اس کا حکم تو ۔ دونوں جمع ہو سکتے ہیں۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں ایک مستقل مسئلہ مذکور ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ لعان کرنے والے شخص نے تفریق قاضی کے بعد جب اپنے آپ کو جھٹلایا یعنی اپنے قول سے رجوع کیا تو اس پر حد تذف واجب ہوگی۔ لیکن اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ اپنی متلاعنہ بیوی سے دوبارہ نکاح کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں تو اس بارے میں طرفین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جس طرح دوسرے کے لئے اس عورت سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح اس کے لئے بھی جائز ہے اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ با ہمی لعان کرنے سے حرمت موبدہ ثابت ہو جاتی ہے لہذا یہ عورت اس کے لئے ہمیشہ حرام رہے گی ۔ یہی قول ہے امام زفر ، حسن اور امام شافعی کا ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور کا ارشاد ہے المتلاعنان لا يجتمعان ابدا یعنی اعان کرنے والے میاں ، بیوی کبھی جمع نہ ہوں گے اس حدیث میں دائمی حرمت پر صراحت کی گئی ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلانا اپنے قول سے رجوع کرنا ہے اور رجوع کرنے کے بعد شہادت کا حکم باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور حدیث کا مطلب بھی یہ ہے کہ جب تک وہ دونوں لعان کرنے والے ہیں تو جمع نہیں ہو سکتے اور اپنے آپ کو جھٹلانے کے بعد نہ با ہمی لعان باقی رہا اور نہ اس کا حکم ۔ اپنی تکذیب کے بعد حقیقت لعان کا باقی نہ رہنا تو ظاہر ہے اور لعان کا حکم اس لئے باقی نہیں رہا کہ جب اس نے اپنی تکذیب کی تو اس پر حد واجب ہوگئی لہذا لعان کی اہلیت ہی باطل ہو گئی اور جب اہلیت لعان باطل ہوگئی تو اس کا حکم ہی باطل ہو گیا۔ اس وجہ سے دونوں جمع
ہو سکتے ہیں۔
Chapter of Li'an. 148. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 5: ...and they will not be together as long as both are engaged in li'an, and after he has contradicted himself, neither the li'an nor its ruling remains. So both can be together. Commentary: In this passage, an independent issue is mentioned. That is: After the judge's separation, when the person who performed li'an contradicts himself, i.e., retracts his statement, then the hadd of qadhf becomes obligatory on him. But there is a difference of opinion on whether he can remarry his mu'tallinah wife. Regarding this, the madhhab of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that just as it is permissible for another to marry this woman, similarly it is permissible for him. Imam Abu Yusuf said: By mutual li'an, a permanent prohibition is established, so this woman will remain forbidden to him forever. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar, Hasan, and Imam al-Shafi'i. The evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the Prophet said: 'The two who perform li'an will never be together.' This hadith clearly indicates permanent prohibition. The evidence of the two is that the husband's contradiction of himself is a retraction of his statement, and after retraction, the ruling of testimony becomes void. The meaning of the hadith is also that as long as both are engaged in li'an, they cannot be together, and after contradiction, neither the mutual li'an nor its ruling remains. After his contradiction, the reality of li'an not remaining is clear, and the ruling of li'an does not remain because when he contradicted himself, the hadd became obligatory on him. Hence, the eligibility for li'an became void, and when the eligibility for li'an became void, its ruling became void. For this reason, both can be together.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of retracting li'an. After a couple has undergone li'an and the judge has separated them, if the husband later admits that he lied (i.e., retracts his accusation), he becomes liable for the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf). The question is whether he can remarry his former wife. The text states that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (referred to as 'the two'), the retraction terminates the permanent prohibition, so he may remarry her just as any other man may. Their reasoning is that retracting the accusation nullifies the li'an ruling, because the husband's own testimony is withdrawn, and the hadith 'The two who perform li'an will never be together' applies only while they are still in the state of li'an. Once the husband retracts, he is no longer a mutala'in, so the prohibition lifts. Imam Abu Yusuf, supported by Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Imam al-Shafi'i, holds that the mutual li'an establishes a permanent prohibition (hurmat mu'abbadah) irrespective of retraction. His evidence is the same hadith, interpreting 'never' as absolute. The Hanafi position (of the two) is preferred because the retraction eliminates the basis for the prohibition. The text is a commentary on al-Hidayah, expanding on this dispute.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses.
حد تذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment for false accusation of adultery (eighty lashes).
حرمت موبدہ (hurmat mu'abbadah): Permanent prohibition of marriage, meaning the spouses can never remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, can a husband who retracts his li'an remarry his former wife?
A) Yes, because retraction voids the li'an ruling.
B) No, because li'an establishes permanent prohibition.
C) Yes, but only after paying compensation.
D) No, unless the wife agrees.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, retracting li'an ends the marital prohibition, but the retractor must still face the hadd punishment for false accusation.

Li'an for Denial of Paternity
Describes the form of li'an when the accusation is denial of a child's paternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the form of li'an when the husband denies paternity and identify the legal consequences for the child's lineage.

Core Idea
Li'an for paternity denial: judge severs child's lineage from husband, attaches to mother; oaths confirm the accusation.

In this passage, we learn the specific wording required for li'an when the accusation is denial of a child. This procedure permanently severs the marital bond and redefines the child's lineage. Understanding the exact form ensures the legal effects are properly executed and the husband avoids punishment for false accusation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the accusation type
The husband's accusation is not direct zina but denial of paternity. Recognize that this is a specific form of qadhf (defamation). The passage says: 'if the accusation is by denial of the child.'
This is distinct from a general accusation of adultery.
2
State the legal consequences
The judge must deny the child's lineage from the husband and attach the child to the mother. The passage states: 'the judge denies the child's lineage and attaches the child to his mother.'
This is immediate upon the accusation, pending li'an.
3
Describe the husband's oath
The ruler instructs the husband to say: 'I testify by Allah that I am indeed among the truthful in what I have accused you of, namely the denial of the child.' This is the first of four oaths, followed by a fifth invoking a curse if he is lying.
The wording explicitly mentions 'denial of the child'.
4
Describe the wife's oath
The wife responds with four oaths that the husband is lying, using similar wording: 'I testify by Allah that you are among the liars in what you have accused me of, namely the denial of the child.' She then swears a fifth invoking Allah's wrath if he is truthful.
Her oath mirrors his, confirming her denials.
5
Summarize the effect
After the full li'an, the marriage is permanently dissolved, the child's lineage is exclusively from the mother, and the husband is freed from the hadd punishment for qadhf.
The father loses all parental rights over the child.

Source Text

اگر تہت بچے کی نفی کی ہو قاضی بچے کے نسب کی نفی کردے اور بچے کو ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کر دے اور لعان کی صورت
ولو كان القذف بنفى الولد نفى القاضى نسبه و الحقه بامه وصورة اللعان ان يأمر الحاكم الرجل فيقول اشهد بالله انى لمن الصادقین فیما رمیتک به من نفى الولدو كذا في جانب المرأة
ترجمہ اور اگر تہمت لگانا بچہ کی نفی کرنے کے ذریعہ سے ہے تو قاضی اس بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کر دے گا اور اس بچہ کو اس کی ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کرے گا اور لعان کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ حاکم اس مرد کو حکم دے وہ کہے کہ میں اللہ کی قسم کے ساتھ گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ میں سچ بولنے والوں میں سے ہوں ۔ اس بات میں کہ میں نے تجھ کو بچہ کی نفی کرنے کا عیب لگا یا اور یہی عورت کی جانب میں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کا عیب اس طرح لگایا کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے۔ تو لعان کے بعد قاضی بچہ کا نسب اس مرد سے نفی کر دے گا اور بچہ کو ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کرے گا اور اس میں لعان کی صورت یہ ہے کہ حاکم اس مرد کو حکم دے کہ وہ یہ کہے میں اللہ کی قسم کے ساتھ گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ میں نے بچہ کی نفی کر کے جو زنا کا عیب لگایا اس میں میں سچا ہوں اور عورت یوں کہے گی کہ
میں اللہ کی قسم کے ساتھ گواہی دیتی ہوں کہ تو نے جو مجھے بچہ کی نفی کا عیب لگا یا اس بات میں تو جھوٹ بولنے والوں میں سے ہے۔
If the accusation is by denial of the child, the judge denies the child's lineage and attaches the child to his mother. And the form of li'an is that the ruler orders the man to say: 'I testify by Allah that I am indeed among the truthful in what I have accused you of, namely the denial of the child.' And similarly on the woman's side. Translation: And if the accusation is through denial of the child, the judge will deny the lineage of that child and attach that child to his mother. And the form of li'an is that the ruler commands the man, he says: 'I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in this matter that I have accused you of the fault of denying the child.' And similarly on the woman's side. Commentary: The issue is that if a person accuses his wife of adultery in such a way that he says this child is not from my semen, then after li'an, the judge will deny the child's lineage from that man and attach the child to the mother. In this, the form of li'an is that the ruler commands the man to say: 'I testify by Allah that I am truthful in accusing you of adultery by denying the child.' And the woman will say: 'I testify by Allah that you are among the liars in what you have accused me of the fault of denying the child.'
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage explains the specific form of li'an when the husband's accusation is that his wife's child is not his. The text states that the judge must deny the child's lineage from the husband and instead attribute the child to the mother. The li'an procedure begins with the ruler instructing the husband to take four oaths that he is truthful in his accusation, followed by a fifth oath invoking Allah's curse if he is lying. The wife similarly takes four oaths that he is lying, and a fifth invoking Allah's wrath if he is truthful. The wording provided is explicit: the husband says he is truthful in accusing her of adultery by denying the child; the wife says he is lying. This is a ruling statement describing the prescribed procedure, suitable for memorization.

Key Terms
نفی ولد (nafy al-walad): Denial of a child's paternity by the husband.
لاحق کرنا (lahiq karna): To attach or attribute a child to its mother (for lineage purposes).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'I testify by Allah that she committed adultery.'
B) 'I testify by Allah that I am truthful in accusing you of adultery by denying the child.'
C) 'I divorce you three times.'
D) 'I am not the father of this child.'

Key Takeaway
Li'an for denial of paternity requires the husband to swear four oaths that he is truthful in accusing her of adultery by denying the child, followed by a curse, and the wife must respond with four oaths that he is lying, followed by an oath of wrath.

Combining Accusation of Zina and Denial of Paternity in Li'an
Ruling with proof from hadith of Hilal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining zina accusation and paternity denial in li'an, apply it to a scenario, and cite the evidence from the hadith of Hilal.

Core Idea
Li'an must explicitly mention both zina and denial of paternity — the Prophet's sunna establishes combined procedure.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in li'an: when a husband accuses his wife of adultery and simultaneously denies the paternity of her child. The Hanafi school holds that both accusations must be included in the li'an procedure, and the judge then denies the child's lineage from the husband and attaches it to the mother. The proof is the well-known hadith of Hilal ibn Umayyah, which the text details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the li'an when both zina and denial of paternity are alleged. The ruling is that mentioning both is wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith of Hilal ibn Umayyah (Ibn Abbas), which describes the Prophet performing li'an and then denying the child's lineage from Hilal and attaching it to the mother.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action shows that both matters are handled together in a single li'an. The denial of lineage and attachment to mother are part of the same procedure, establishing the combined rule.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the judge must explicitly state the denial and attachment in words, while the majority view is that the judge's ruling suffices without explicit phrasing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Abu Yusuf, if the judge does not explicitly pronounce, the denial may not be effective; according to the majority, it is effective. The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہی
۱۴۹
باب اللعان
اگر تہمت زنا کی ہو اور بچے کی نفی کرے تو لعان میں دو باتوں کا تذکرہ کیا جائے
پھر اس بچے کے نسب کی نفی کرے اور ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کرے
ولو قذفها بالزنا و نفى الولد ذكر فى اللعان الامرين ثم ينفى القاضى نسب الولد ويلحقه بامه لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام نفى ولد امرأة هلال بن امية عن هلال والحقه بها ولان المقصود من هذا اللعان نفى الولد فيوفر عليه مقصوده فيتضمنة القضاء بالتفريق وعن ابى يوسف ان القاضى يفرق ويقول قد الزمته امه واخرجته من نسب الاب لانه ينفك عنه فلابد من ذكره
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر نے بیوی کو نا ک اور بچہ کی نفی کا عیب لگایا تو لعان میں دونوں باتیں ذکر کی جاویں پھر قاضی اس بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کمر کے اس کی ماں کے ساتھ ملحق کرے۔ کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہلال بن امیہ کی بیوی کے بچہ ( کا نسب ) بلال سے قطع کر کے اس کی ماں سے لاحق کیا اور اس لئے بھی کہ اس لعان سے مقصود یہ ہے کہ بچہ کی نفی ہو تو شوہر کا مقصود اس سے پورا حاصل ہوجائے گا پس جدا کرنے کا فیصلہ اس کو شامل ہوگا اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ قاضی تفریق کرے اور یہ کہ میں نے بچہ اس کی ماں کو لازم کیا اور باپ کے نسب سے اس کو خارج کیا کیوں کہ بچہ کی نفی تفریق سے جدا ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے اس کا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کا عیب لگایا اور بچہ کی نفی کرتے ہوئے کہا یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو
لعان میں دونوں باتیں ذکر کی جاویں پھر قاضی باپ سے اس بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کر کے اس کی ماں کے ساتھ لاحق کر دے۔
دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو ابن عباس سے روایت ہے۔ خادم آپ کی دلچسپی کے لئے پوری حدیث نقل کرتا ہے۔
عذاب
قال جاء هلال بن اميه وهو احد الثلاثة الذين تاب الله عليهم فجاء من ارضه عشاء فوجد عند اهله رجلا فرأى بعينه و سمع باذنيه فلم يهجه حتى اصبح ثم غدا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله اني جنت اهلى عشاء فوجدت عندهم رجلا فرأیت بعینی و سمعت باذنی فکره رسول الله ما جاء به واشتد عليه فنزلت والذين يرمون ازواجهم و لم يكن لهم شهداء الا انفسهم فشهادة احدهم الأيتين كلتيهما فسرى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال ابشر يا هلال قد جعل الله لک فرجا و مخرجا قال هلال قد كنت ارجو ذالك من ربی فقال رسول الله ارسلوا اليها فجائت فتلا عليها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و ذكرهما اخبرهما ان عذاب الآخرة اشد من الدنياء فقال هلال والله لقد صدقت عليها فقالت قد كذب فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا عنوا بينهما فقيل لهلال اشهد فشهد اربع شهادات بالله انه ممن الصادقين فلما كانت الخمسة قيل يا هلال اتق الله فان عقاب الدنيا اهون من عذاب الآخرة. و ان هذه الموجبة التي توجب عليك والعذاب فقال والله لا يعذبنى الله عليها كما لم يجلدنى عليها فشهد الخامسة ان لعنة الله عليه ان كان من الكاذبين ثم قيل لها اشهدى فشهدت اربع شهادات بالله انه من الكاذبين فلما كانت الخامسة قيل لها اتقى الله فان عذاب الدنيا اهون من عذاب الأخرة و ان هذه الموجبة التي توجب
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 5. 149. Chapter of Li'an. If the accusation is of adultery and he denies the child, then in the li'an, both matters are mentioned. Then he denies the lineage of that child and attaches it to the mother. And if he accuses her of adultery and denies the child, both matters are mentioned in the li'an. Then the judge denies the lineage of the child and attaches it to the mother, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) denied the child of the wife of Hilal ibn Umayyah from Hilal and attached it to her. And because the purpose of this li'an is the denial of the child, so his purpose is fulfilled, and it includes the ruling of separation. And from Abu Yusuf: that the judge separates and says: 'I have made the child attached to his mother and removed him from the father's lineage,' because the denial of the child is separate from separation, so it must be mentioned. Commentary: The scenario is that if the husband accused his wife of adultery and said, 'This child is not from my semen,' then in the li'an, both matters are mentioned. Then the judge denies the child's lineage from the father and attaches it to the mother. Evidence: The hadith narrated by Ibn Abbas. The servant narrates the full hadith for your interest. Punishment. He said: Hilal ibn Umayyah came, and he was one of the three whom Allah forgave. He came from his land in the evening and found a man with his family. He saw with his eye and heard with his ear, but did not disturb him until morning. Then he went to the Messenger of Allah and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I came to my family in the evening and found a man with them, I saw with my eye and heard with my ear.' The Messenger disliked what he brought and it was hard on him. Then the verse was revealed: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves, then the testimony of one of them is four testimonies...' (Quran 24:6). Then the Messenger was relieved and said, 'Rejoice, O Hilal, Allah has made for you a way out.' Hilal said, 'I was hoping for that from my Lord.' The Messenger said, 'Send for her.' She came, and the Messenger recited to her and mentioned both of them, informing them that the punishment of the Hereafter is more severe than that of this world. Hilal said, 'By Allah, I have spoken the truth about her.' She said, 'He has lied.' The Messenger said, 'Perform li'an between them.' So it was said to Hilal, 'Testify,' and he testified four times by Allah that he is among the truthful. When it came to the fifth, it was said, 'O Hilal, fear Allah, for the punishment of this world is lighter than the punishment of the Hereafter, and this is the binding oath that gives you the punishment.' He said, 'By Allah, Allah will not punish me for it just as He did not flog me for it.' So he testified the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he was among the liars. Then it was said to her, 'Testify,' and she testified four times by Allah that he is among the liars. When it came to the fifth, it was said to her, 'Fear Allah, for the punishment of this world is lighter than the punishment of the Hereafter, and this is the binding oath that gives you...'
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a husband accuses his wife of adultery and simultaneously denies the paternity of her child. The ruling is that the li'an procedure must explicitly mention both accusations: the zina and the denial of paternity. The judge then nullifies the child's lineage from the husband and attributes the child to the mother. The proof provided is the hadith of Hilal ibn Umayyah, one of the three whose repentance was accepted (the others being Ka'b ibn Malik and Murarah ibn al-Rabi'). The hadith details the incident that led to the revelation of the li'an verses in Surah al-Nur (24:6-9). The Prophet performed li'an between Hilal and his wife, and after the li'an, the child was attributed to the mother, not to Hilal. The text also mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf that the judge should explicitly state in the ruling that the child is attached to the mother and removed from the father's lineage. The passage is incomplete as it cuts off mid-hadith.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation between spouses as a result of li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a husband alleges both zina and denial of paternity, the li'an must include both accusations, and the judge denies the child's lineage from the husband and attaches it to the mother, as established by the sunna.

Retracting Li'an: Hadd and Remarriage
Ruling with proof on retraction of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband retracts his li'an and confesses falsehood, identify the hadd punishment, and explain why remarriage becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Confession after li'an triggers hadd for qadhf and lifts the permanent prohibition on remarriage.

In the previous lesson, we learned that li'an results in permanent separation. But what if the husband admits his accusation was false? This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the legal consequences: the husband must receive the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf), and after that, he may remarry his former wife. We will walk through the reasoning and its application to analogous cases.

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling
Identify the two key outcomes: (1) the husband is punished with hadd for qadhf, (2) he may remarry the wife.
These outcomes are conditional on the husband retracting his li'an and confessing falsehood.
2
Identify the basis for hadd
The husband's confession (iqrar) that his accusation was false establishes the obligation of hadd. Confession is a binding proof in Hanafi fiqh.
Iqrar is a direct admission; it removes the need for witnesses.
3
Explain the removal of prohibition
After receiving hadd, the husband is no longer eligible for li'an. Since the prohibition on remarriage was a ruling dependent on li'an, it ceases to apply.
The text uses the reason: 'because when he is punished, he is no longer eligible for li'an'.
4
Extend to analogous cases
The text draws analogies: if the husband accused another woman and was punished for qadhf, he may marry her; if the wife committed zina and was punished for zina, the prohibition also ends.
In both cases, the underlying cause (eligibility for li'an) is removed.
5
Note the Hanafi authority
The text states 'this is according to us' (عندنا), referring to the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the school.
Abu Yusuf may have had a different view, but the text presents this as the dominant Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن عاد الزوج وأكذب نفسه حده القاضى لإقراره بوجوب الحد عليه وحل له أن يتزوجها وهذا عندنا لأنه لما حد لم يبق أهل اللعان فارتفع حكمه المنوط به وهو التحريم وكذلك إن قذف غيرها فحدبه لما بينا وكذا إذا زنت فحدت لانتفاء أهلية اللعان من جانبها. پھر اگر شوہر نے رجوع کیا اور اپنے آپ کو جھٹلایا تو قاضی اس کو حد قذف مارے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے اوپر حد واجب ہونے کا اقرار کیا ہے اور اس مرد کے لئے حلال ہے کہ وہ اس عورت سے نکاح کرلے اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے۔ کیونکہ جب اس کو حد ماری گئی تو وہ اہل لعان کے لائق نہیں رہا۔ پس جو حکم اس کے ساتھ متعلق تھا وہ بھی اٹھ گیا اور وہ حکم تحریم ہے اور اسی طرح اگر مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے علاوہ کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی جس کی وجہ سے اس کو حد ماری گئی تو بھی اس کو جائز ہے کہ اس عورت سے نکاح کر لے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب عورت نے زنا کیا، پھر اس کو حد لگائی گئی۔ کیونکہ عورت کی جانب سے لعان کی لیاقت منتفی ہوئی۔
Then if the husband returns and denies himself, the judge imposes the hadd (punishment for qadhf) due to his confession that the hadd is obligatory upon him, and it becomes permissible for him to marry her. And this is according to us, because when he is punished, he is no longer eligible for li'an, so the ruling dependent on it, which is prohibition (tahrim), is removed. Similarly, if he accuses another woman and is punished, it is permissible for him to marry her, due to what we explained. Likewise, if she commits zina and is punished, because her eligibility for li'an is nullified from her side.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the consequences when a husband retracts his li'an (mutual imprecation) and confesses that his accusation was false. The key ruling: the husband is punished with the hadd for qadhf (false accusation of zina) because he has confessed to making a false accusation that warrants the hadd. After this punishment, it becomes permissible for him to remarry his former wife (from whom he was separated by li'an) because the punishment removes his eligibility for li'an, and therefore the prohibition (tahrim) that resulted from the li'an is lifted. This position is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the two companions). The proof is rational: since the hadd eliminates the capacity for li'an, the effect of li'an (the permanent prohibition) also ends. The passage then extends this ruling to two analogous cases: (1) if the husband falsely accuses another woman (not his wife) and receives hadd for qadhf, it also becomes permissible for him to marry that woman; (2) if after li'an the wife commits zina and is punished with the hadd for zina, her eligibility for li'an is removed, so the prohibition also ceases and remarriage becomes permissible.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses; involves oaths and curses.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; a crime punishable by hadd (80 lashes).
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes, e.g., 80 lashes for qadhf.
تحریم (tahrim): Prohibition; here, the prohibition of the husband marrying the wife after li'an.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; here, the husband's confession that his accusation was false.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the immediate consequence when a husband retracts his li'an and confesses falsehood?
A) The judge imposes the hadd for zina (100 lashes)
B) The judge imposes the hadd for qadhf (80 lashes)
C) The marriage is automatically annulled forever
D) The husband must fast for two months

Key Takeaway
Confession after li'an triggers hadd for qadhf and lifts the permanent prohibition on remarriage, based on the removal of li'an eligibility.

No Li'an When Wife is Minor or Insane
Ruling on li'an when wife is minor/insane with qiyas reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that li'an is invalid when the wife is a minor or insane and explain the qiyas reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Li'an is a substitute for hadd; if hadd is inapplicable, li'an is invalid.

The institution of li'an is a unique procedure that replaces the hadd punishment for slander (qadhf) when the accuser is a husband. However, this substitution is contingent on the wife being legally competent for the hadd to be applicable. In this lesson, we examine a key limitation: li'an is not valid when the wife is a minor or insane, based on a clear qiyas (analogical reasoning) from the case of a stranger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the explicit hukm: there is no li'an between them when the wife is a minor or insane.
2
Identify the proof type
Recognize that the proof is qiyas (analogy), as the text compares the husband to a stranger.
3
Analyze the asl (original case)
Consider the case of a stranger accusing a minor or insane woman: the stranger would not receive hadd for qadhf.
The illa (effective cause) is the wife's lack of legal capacity to be the subject of hadd.
4
Apply the illa to the far' (new case)
Since the husband's li'an stands in place of hadd, the same illa applies: the wife's incapacity prevents li'an.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the husband is not called to li'an, as it would be invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قذف امرأته وهى صغيرة أو مجنونة فلا لعان بينهما لأنه لا يحد قاذفها لو كان أجنبيا فكذا لا يلاعن الزوج لقيامه مقامه. اور اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کا عیب لگایا حالانکہ وہ بچی ہے، یا دیوانی ہے تو ان دونوں میں لعان نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد نہیں ماری جاتی اگر چہ اجنبی ہو۔ پس ایسے ہی شوہر سے لعان نہ کرایا جائے اس لئے کہ لعان حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے۔
And if he accuses his wife while she is a minor or insane, then there is no li'an between them, because her accuser would not be punished with hadd if he were a stranger. So likewise the husband should not be made to perform li'an, because li'an stands in the place of hadd for qadhf.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage states a ruling with proof regarding the validity of li'an when the accused wife is a minor or insane. The ruling: li'an does not take place between them. The proof is analogical: if a stranger (non-husband) falsely accused a minor or insane woman of zina, he would not be punished with the hadd for qadhf because the minor and insane are not legally competent for such punishment to apply. Since li'an is a substitute for the hadd of qadhf in the context of a spouse, the same principle applies: the husband should not be made to perform li'an because the fundamental precondition — that the hadd would be applicable for a stranger — is absent. Thus li'an is invalid in this case.

Key Terms
صغيرة (saghirah): A female minor who has not reached puberty and is not legally responsible.
مجنونة (majnunah): An insane woman lacking mental capacity.
قيام مقام (qiyam maqam): Li'an stands in the place of hadd; it is a substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is li'an not valid when the wife is a minor or insane?
A) Because the husband is not allowed to accuse them
B) Because a stranger would not be punished with hadd for accusing them, and li'an is a substitute for hadd
C) Because they cannot give testimony
D) Because the judge does not accept the accusation

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a substitute for hadd; if the hadd would not apply to a stranger, li'an is not valid for the husband.

No Li'an When Husband is Minor, Insane, or Mute
Ruling with proof: extending li'an invalidity to minors, insane, and mute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases where li'an is invalid and explain the Hanafi proof for each.

Core Idea
Li'an requires explicit verbal accusation; a minor, insane, or mute husband cannot fulfill this condition.

This passage extends the previous ruling on li'an to situations where the husband lacks legal capacity or the ability to speak. The text clarifies that li'an, like the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf), is tied to explicit speech (sarih). Therefore, a minor, insane, or mute husband cannot initiate li'an. This lesson examines the reasoning behind each exclusion and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the mute's capability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three excluded cases
The text lists three types of husbands for whom li'an is not valid: minor, insane, and mute. Note the shared and distinct reasons.
Minor and insane share the reason of lacking capacity for testimony; mute has a separate reason.
2
Analyze the proof for minor and insane
They lack ahliyyat al-shahadah (capacity to testify), which is a prerequisite for li'an because li'an involves swearing testimony.
Capacity to testify requires sanity and maturity.
3
Analyze the proof for the mute
Li'an is attached to explicit speech (sarih) like the hadd of qadhf. A mute's communication (signs, writing) is not free from doubt (shubha), and hudud are averted by doubts.
The principle 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' is invoked.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a mute can perform li'an through clear signs or writing. The Hanafi response is that such expression still contains doubt.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of sarih and shubha.
5
Determine practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi practice, a mute husband's accusation never leads to li'an. In Shafi'i practice, it may. This affects whether the wife can defend herself via li'an.
The dispute is solely about the mute; minor and insane are agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا كان الزوج صغيرا أو مجنونا لعدم أهلية الشهادة وقذف الأخرس لا يتعلق به اللعان لأنه يتعلق بالصريح كحد القذف وفيه خلاف الشافعى وهذا لأنه لا يعرى عن الشبهة والحدود تندرئ بها. اور ایسے ہی جب شوہر بچہ ہو یا دیوانہ ہو ( تو بھی لعان نہیں) کیونکہ شوہر میں شہادت کی لیاقت نہیں ہے۔ اور گونگے کا تہمت لگانا اس کے ساتھ بھی لعان متعلق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ لعان صریح قذف سے متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ حد قذف اور اس میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ گونگے کا کہنا شبہ سے خالی نہیں اور حدود شبہات کی وجہ سے دور کر دی جاتی ہیں۔
And likewise when the husband is a minor or insane, due to lack of capacity for testimony. And the accusation of a mute person is not connected to li'an, because li'an is connected to explicit speech, like the hadd of qadhf. And there is a difference of opinion with al-Shafi'i. And this is because his speech is not free from doubt, and legal punishments (hudud) are warded off by doubts.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage covers three cases where li'an is not valid due to the husband's incapacity: (1) if the husband is a minor, (2) if he is insane, and (3) if he is mute. For the minor and insane, the proof is that they lack the capacity to give testimony (shahadah), which is a prerequisite for li'an. For the mute, li'an is not attached to his accusation because li'an requires explicit speech (sarih) — clear verbal accusation of zina. A mute's expression (through writing or signs) is not considered explicit enough, and the hadd of qadhf also requires explicit speech. Imam al-Shafi'i differed on this, holding that a mute's accusation can lead to li'an. The Hanafi justification is that a mute's communication is not free from doubt (shubha), and hudud punishments (including the substitute li'an) are averted by doubts.

Key Terms
أهلية الشهادة (ahliyyat al-shahadah): Legal capacity to give testimony; requires sanity, maturity, and ability to speak clearly.
صريح (sarih): Explicit, unambiguous speech; li'an requires clear verbal accusation.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or uncertainty that prevents the application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a mute husband not perform li'an according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a mute cannot speak, and li'an requires explicit speech
B) Because a mute is not considered legally responsible
C) Because a mute's accusation is always rejected
D) Because li'an is only for sane adults

Key Takeaway
Li'an requires explicit verbal speech; therefore a minor, insane, or mute husband cannot perform it.

Li'an of a Dumb Person: The Requirement of Explicit Verbal Qadhf
Explains a madhhab dispute over li'an for the mute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that li'an requires explicit verbal qadhf and identify the Shafi'i counter-argument based on equivalence of gesture to speech.

Core Idea
Li'an is linked to explicit qadhf; a dumb person's gesture involves doubt, so no li'an.

When a dumb husband accuses his wife of zina through gestures, can the couple undergo li'an? The Hanafi school says no, because li'an is tied to explicit verbal accusation, just like hadd for qadhf. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, equating gestures with speech. This lesson dissects the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested act and the Hanafi ruling
The act is li'an initiated by a dumb person through gestures. The Hanafi ruling is that li'an is not valid.
The ruling is based on the absence of explicit verbal qadhf.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof (qiyas)
The proof is analogical: just as hadd for qadhf is only incurred by explicit words, li'an (which leads to separation and negation of lineage) is also only linked to explicit words.
This is qiyas jaliy: the common illa is 'explicit accusation'.
3
Understand the Shafi'i opposing proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a dumb person's gesture is equivalent to speech (isharat al-akhras ka-kalam al-natiq), so it should suffice for li'an.
The Shafi'i rely on the general rule that gestures of the mute substitute for speech in legal acts.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response invokes the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubuhat). The gesture of a dumb person carries doubt (shubha) because it may be misinterpreted, so hadd and li'an are not established.
The doubt is intrinsic to the medium of communication.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: no li'an, so marriage continues and lineage is not negated. Shafi'i: li'an takes place, resulting in separation and negation of the child's lineage.
This difference has real consequences for the couple and any children.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر گونگے نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کا عیب لگایا تو اس سے بھی لعان متعلق نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لعان صریح قذف سے متعلق ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ حد قذف صریح قذف سے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس میں امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ گونگے کا اشارہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ بولنے والے کا کلام کرنا اور گونگے کے اشارے سے لعان کا واجب نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ گونگے کے زنا کا عیب لگانے میں شبہ موجود ہے اور شبہات کی وجہ سے حدود دور کر دی جاتی ہیں۔
And if a dumb person accuses his wife of zina, then li'an will not be related to him either. The proof is that li'an is related to explicit qadhf, just as the hadd of qadhf is obligatory due to explicit qadhf. Imam al-Shafi'i differs; he says that the gesture of a dumb person is like the speech of a speaking person. And the reason li'an is not obligatory by the dumb person's gesture is that there is doubt in the dumb person's accusation of zina, and hudud are averted due to doubts.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of li'an when a dumb person (who cannot speak) accuses his wife of zina through gestures. The Hanafi position is that li'an does not occur because li'an is only linked to explicit verbal qadhf, just as the hadd punishment for qadhf is only obligatory with explicit words. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that a dumb person's gesture is equivalent to speech. The Hanafi response is that the gesture of a dumb person involves doubt, and the principle is that hudud (punishments) are averted by doubts. The passage follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the proof (qiyas to hadd qadhf), then the opposing view of Shafi'i, and finally the Hanafi justification for the ruling.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A mutual oath of imprecation between spouses when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, leading to separation.
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a married person of zina, which incurs hadd punishment unless proven.
صریح قذف (sarih qadhf): Explicit verbal accusation of zina without any ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a dumb person not incur li'an according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because he cannot speak at all.
B) Because his gesture involves doubt (shubha), and hudud are averted by doubts.
C) Because li'an is only for speaking persons.
D) Because the wife's consent is required.

Key Takeaway
Li'an requires explicit verbal qadhf; a dumb person's gesture involves doubt, so li'an is not established.

Denial of Pregnancy and the Requirement of Li'an
Intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an requirement after denial of pregnancy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the issue of li'an upon denial of pregnancy, and evaluate the reasoning (illah) of each side.

Core Idea
Denial of pregnancy does not trigger li'an if it is conditional on uncertain pregnancy — qadhf cannot be conditional.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the legal effect of a husband's statement 'Your pregnancy is not from me.' The issue is whether this statement amounts to qadhf (false accusation of zina) requiring li'an (mutual imprecation). The scholars differ based on the certainty of pregnancy at the moment of utterance and the validity of conditional qadhf. In this lesson, we will carefully parse the arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling and its proponents
The passage opens with the ruling: no li'an. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar. Note that it is presented as the default, suggesting it is the relied-upon position in the base text.
The statement 'ليس حملک مني' is not considered qadhf at the moment because pregnancy is not certain.
2
Recognize the condition introduced by the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani add a condition: if the wife gives birth within less than six months from the time of the statement, then li'an becomes obligatory. They argue that the birth retroactively confirms pregnancy existed at the time, making the denial a definitive accusation.
The six-month period is based on the minimum duration of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa
At the time of the statement, the existence of pregnancy is not certain—it could be wind in the belly. Therefore, the husband is not a qadhif (accuser). The statement is effectively conditional, as if he said 'If you are pregnant, it is not from me.'
Conditional qadhf is invalid in Hanafi usul because qadhf requires a definitive, unconditional accusation.
4
Analyze the proof of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn rely on retroactive certainty: the birth within six months proves that pregnancy was indeed present at the time of the denial. Thus, the husband's statement becomes a definite accusation of zina, triggering li'an.
This reasoning is based on the principle that a later event can clarify the status at an earlier time (kashf).
5
Synthesize the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
The commentator defends Abu Hanifa by reiterating that the statement is conditional and qadhf cannot be conditional. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, no li'an and no separation; under the Sahibayn, if the birth occurs within six months, li'an occurs leading to perpetual prohibition and negation of lineage.
Some later Hanafi authorities prefer the view of Abu Hanifa as it avoids unnecessary li'an proceedings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قال الزوج ليس حملک منى فلا لعان وهذا قول أبي حنيفة وزفر لانه لا يتيقن بقيام الحمل فلم يصر قاذفا وقال ابويوسف ومحمد اللعان يجب بنفى الحمل اذاجاء ت به لاقل من ستة اشهر وهو معنى ما ذكر في الأصل لانا تيقنا بقيام الحمل عنده فيتحقق القذف قلنا اذا لم يكن قذفا في الحال يصير كالمعلق بالشرط فيصير كانه قال ان کان بک حمل فليس منى والقذف لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط. تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ تیرا حمل مجھ سے نہیں ہے تو اس سے نہ لعان واجب ہوگا اور نہ حد اور یہ لعان واجب نہ ہونا امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام زفر کا قول ہے اور یہی قول ہے امام احمد کا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر اس عورت نے تہمت لگانے کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا تو حمل کی نفی کر دینے سے لعان واجب ہو جائے گا اور یہ چھ ماہ سے کم کی قید مبسوط میں بھی مذکور ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس وقت حمل کی نفی کی گئی اس وقت حمل کا ہونا یقینی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ پیٹ میں ہوا بھری ہو جس کو حمل خیال کیا اس وجہ سے شوہر تہمت لگانے والا شمار نہیں ہو گا اور جب قذف ثابت نہیں ہوا تو لعان واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب قذف کرنے کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو ہم کو یقین ہو گیا کہ قذف کے وقت حمل موجود تھا تو تہمت لگانا پایا گیا اور جب تہمت لگانا پایا گیا تو شوہر پر لعان واجب ہوگا۔ مگر ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہوگا کہ شوہر کا قول ليس حملک منی فی الحال تو قذف نہیں ہوا کیونکہ فی الحال وجود حمل متیقن نہیں ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ شرط پر معلق کیا گیا شوہر نے کہا ان کان بکہ حمل فلیس منی یعنی اگر تو حاملہ ہے تو وہ حمل مجھ سے نہیں اور قذف کو شرط پر معلق کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ قذف نہیں ہوگا اور جب قذف نہیں ہوا تو لعان بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
And if the husband says, 'Your pregnancy is not from me,' then there is no li'an. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Zufar because he is not certain of the existence of pregnancy, so he does not become a qadhif. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Li'an is obligatory by negating the pregnancy when she brings a child in less than six months, and this is the meaning mentioned in al-Asl, because we became certain of the existence of pregnancy at that time, so qadhf is realized. We reply: Since it was not qadhf at the time, it becomes like something conditional, as if he said, 'If you are pregnant, it is not from me,' and qadhf is not valid when conditional. Explanation: If the husband says to his wife, 'Your pregnancy is not from me,' then neither li'an nor hadd is obligatory. This ruling of no li'an is the view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar, and it is also the view of Ahmad. The Sahibayn said: If the woman gives birth in less than six months from the time of accusation, then by negating pregnancy, li'an becomes obligatory. This condition of less than six months is also mentioned in al-Mabsut. The proof of Abu Hanifa and Zufar is that at the time of negation, the existence of pregnancy is not certain, because it is possible that the belly is filled with air mistaken for pregnancy, so the husband is not considered an accuser, and when qadhf is not proven, li'an is not obligatory. The proof of the Sahibayn is that when the child is born in less than six months from the time of qadhf, we become certain that pregnancy existed at the time of qadhf, so the accusation is established, and when accusation is established, li'an is obligatory upon the husband. However, our response is that the husband's statement 'Your pregnancy is not from me' is not qadhf at the time because the existence of pregnancy is not certain at that time. Thus it becomes like something conditional: the husband said, 'If you are pregnant, then it is not from me,' and qadhf cannot be made conditional. So it is not qadhf, and li'an is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the statement 'Your pregnancy is not from me.' The text first presents the ruling: no li'an, which is the view of Abu Hanifa and Zufar. Then it presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) that li'an becomes obligatory if the wife gives birth within less than six months from the time of the statement. The passage then details the reasoning for each side. Abu Hanifa and Zufar argue that at the time of the statement, pregnancy is not certain; there could be doubt (e.g., wind in the belly). The Sahibayn argue that if birth occurs within six months, it retroactively confirms pregnancy at the time of the statement, so qadhf is realized. However, the Hanafi response (from the commentator's perspective) is that the statement is conditional: it is as if he said 'If you are pregnant, it is not from me,' and qadhf cannot be conditional, so li'an is not valid. The passage ends with a detailed explanation (tashrih) restating the positions. This lesson is a parsing exercise because it requires careful distinction between the views and their proofs.

Key Terms
نفی حمل (nafy al-haml): The husband's denial that the pregnancy is from him, which can lead to li'an if conditions are met.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) against a married person.
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses; leads to separation and negation of lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he did not use the word 'zina'.
B) Because pregnancy is not certain at the time of the statement, so it is like a conditional statement.
C) Because the wife must first give birth.
D) Because li'an is only for speaking persons.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a husband's denial of paternity does not automatically trigger li'an unless the statement is clearly an accusation of zina without condition or doubt.

10 min
Husband Explicitly Says 'You Committed Zina and This Pregnancy is from Zina'
Ruling that li'an occurs and qadi does not negate lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies immediate negation of lineage during pregnancy in li'an, and refute the Shafi'i counter-proof using the Hadith of Hilal.

Core Idea
Lineage is not negated before birth because rulings depend on certainty, and pregnancy itself is not certain.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah addresses a critical dispute: when a husband explicitly accuses his wife of zina and states the pregnancy is from zina, does the qadi immediately negate the child's lineage? The Hanafi school holds that lineage remains intact until after birth, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues for immediate negation based on the precedent of Hilal. Understanding this disagreement requires careful analysis of the hadith and the Hanafi principle of suspending rulings until certainty.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The qadi does not negate the lineage of the unborn child; li'an occurs but lineage is preserved until after birth.
This is based on the principle that rulings concerning the child apply only after birth.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the qadi should negate the lineage immediately during pregnancy.
His evidence is the Hadith of Hilal.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Hadith of Hilal: The Prophet negated the child from Hilal while the wife was pregnant.
This seems to directly support immediate negation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes the hadith as specific to revelation; the general principle is that rulings about the child apply only after birth due to doubt before birth.
The Prophet knew through revelation, so the case is exceptional.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In Hanafi, the child is born with the husband's lineage until li'an after birth; in Shafi'i, lineage is negated immediately, affecting inheritance and other rights.
The dispute has real-world consequences for the child's status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قال لهاز نيت وهذا الحبل من الزناء تلاعنا لوجود القذف حيث ذكر الزناء صريحا ولم ينف القاضي الحمل وقال الشافعي ينفيه لانه عليه السلام نفى الولد عن هلال وقد قذفها حاملا ولنا ان الاحكام لاتترتب عليه الابعد الولادة لتمكن الاحتمال قبله والحديث محمول على انه عرف قيام الحبل بطريق الوحي. تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ تو نے زنا کیا ہے اور یہ حمل زنا سے ہے تو اس صورت میں میاں بیوی دونوں لعان کریں گے دلیل یہ ہے کہ صراحتا لفظ زنا کے کہنے کی وجہ سے زنا کا عیب لگانا پایا گیا۔ البتہ قاضی اس حمل کے نسب کی نفی نہیں کرے گا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی حمل کے نسب کی نفی کر دے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور نے ہلال سے عورت کے بچہ کی نفی کی تھی ، حالانکہ ہلال نے اس عورت کو حاملہ ہونے کی حالت میں عیب لگایا تھا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ کی نفی کرنا بچہ کے احکام میں سے ایک حکم ہے اور احکام ولد مرتب ہوتے ہیں ولادت کے بعد نہ کہ ولادت سے پہلے اس لئے کہ ولادت سے پہلے شبہ موجود ہے۔ یعنی ہو سکتا ہے کہ حمل نہ ہو بلکہ مرض سے خون جم گیا ہو۔ اور حدیث ہلال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث اس بات پر محمول ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حمل موجود وحی کے ذریعہ سے علم کر لیا تھا اور قرینہ اس پر یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اگر بچہ ایسی اور ایسی شکل کا ہو تو ہلال کا ہے اور اگر ایسی اور ایسی شکل کا ہو تو شریک بن شما کا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بات بطریق وحی ہی کہی جاسکتی ہے۔
If he says, 'You committed zina and this pregnancy is from zina,' then both perform li'an due to the existence of qadhf, since he mentioned zina explicitly, and the qadi does not negate the pregnancy. Al-Shafi'i said: He does negate it, because the Prophet negated the child from Hilal, even though Hilal accused her while she was pregnant. Our proof: Rulings are not established upon it except after birth, because probability exists before it. The hadith is interpreted to mean that he knew of the existence of pregnancy through revelation. Explanation: If the husband says to his wife, 'You committed zina and this pregnancy is from zina,' then in this case both spouses perform li'an. The proof is that due to the explicit mention of the word 'zina', the accusation of zina is established. However, the qadi will not negate the lineage of this pregnancy. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the qadi should negate the lineage of the pregnancy. His proof is that the Prophet negated the child from Hilal, even though Hilal accused his wife while she was pregnant. Our proof is that negating the child is one of the rulings concerning the child, and rulings of the child are established after birth, not before, because before birth there is doubt. That is, it is possible that it is not a pregnancy but rather blood clotted due to disease. The response to the hadith of Hilal is that it is interpreted to mean that the Prophet knew of the existence of pregnancy through revelation. An indication of this is that the Prophet said, 'If the child has such and such appearance, it is from Hilal; if it has such and such appearance, it is from Sharik ibn Sam'a,' and it is obvious that he could only say that through revelation.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a husband explicitly states, 'You committed zina and this pregnancy is from zina.' The Hanafi position is that li'an takes place because the accusation is explicit, but the qadi does not negate the lineage of the unborn child until after birth. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that lineage should be negated immediately, based on the hadith of Hilal. The Hanafi response distinguishes: rulings regarding the child (including negation of lineage) only apply after birth because before birth there is probability (e.g., maybe it's not pregnancy but a medical condition). The hadith of Hilal is interpreted as a special case where the Prophet knew through revelation that the pregnancy was from zina. The commentator then provides a detailed explanation (tashrih) confirming the Hanafi position. This is an inter-madhhab dispute with clear proof and counterproof.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A mutual oath of condemnation between spouses when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses.
قذف (qadhf): Accusation of zina; the act that triggers li'an.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity of a child, which is negated through li'an after birth in Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school say the qadi does not negate the lineage of the unborn child when li'an is performed during pregnancy?
A) Because the husband did not explicitly accuse the wife.
B) Because rulings concerning the child are only established after birth, as there is doubt before birth.
C) Because the wife must consent.
D) Because li'an cannot be performed during pregnancy.

Key Takeaway
Explicit accusation of zina during pregnancy triggers li'an, but the negation of lineage is deferred until after birth due to the possibility of doubt before birth.

Timing of Paternity Denial: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity denial timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the valid time for denying paternity and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The timing of paternity denial is tied to the husband's conduct, not a fixed period.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the window for a husband to deny paternity of his wife's newborn. Abu Hanifa ties the validity to immediate action or acceptance of congratulations/purchase of birth tools, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad extend it to the entire postnatal period (nifas). Understanding this dispute reveals how the school balances textual indicators and real-world circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage deals with the valid time for a husband to deny paternity of his wife's child. This is a dispute about timing, not the act of denial itself.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that denial is valid only immediately after birth or at the time when congratulations are accepted or birth tools are purchased. Delayed denial does not negate lineage.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say denial is valid throughout the postnatal period (nifas), which is typically 40 days. They argue that a short period is appropriate, and nifas is the natural limit.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues against a fixed time because people's circumstances differ; the indicator should be the husband's conduct at the time of congratulations—whether he accepted, remained silent, or purchased tools.
5
Analyse the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn reason that denial is only valid in a short period, and nifas serves as a clear, objective boundary based on the effect of birth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا نفسى الرجل ولد امرأته عقيب الولادة او فى الحالة التي تقبل التهنية وتبتاع آلة الولادة صح نفيه ولاعن به وان نفاه بعد ذلك لاعن ويثبت النسب هذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابويوسف ومحمد يصح نفيه في مدة النفاس لان النفى يصح في مدة قصيرة ولا يصح في مدة طويلة ففصلنا بينهما يمدة النفاس لانه اثر الولادة وله انه لا معنى للتقدير لان الزمان للتامل و احوال الناس فيه مختلفة فاعتبر نامايدل عليه وهو قبوله التهنية او سكوته عند التهنية او ابتياعه متاع الولادة او مضى ذلك الوقت وهو ممتنع عن النفى
And if a man denies the child of his wife immediately after birth or in the situation where congratulations are accepted and the tools of birth are purchased, his denial is valid and he performs li'an because of it. If he denies after that, he performs li'an and the lineage is established. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: His denial is valid within the period of postnatal bleeding (nifas), because denial is valid in a short period and not valid in a long period, so we differentiate between them by the period of nifas because it is the effect of birth. And for him (Abu Hanifa) there is no meaning in estimation, because time is for reflection and the circumstances of people differ; so we consider what indicates it, which is his acceptance of congratulations or his silence at congratulations or his purchase of birth tools or the passage of that time while he refrains from denial.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valid time for a husband to deny paternity of his wife's newborn child. According to Abu Hanifa, the denial is valid only if done immediately after birth, or at the time when congratulations are received and birth tools are purchased. If he delays beyond that, he loses the right to deny, and if he attempts denial later, li'an is performed but the lineage is already established. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad extend the period to the entire postnatal period (nifas), reasoning that denial is only valid within a short period. Abu Hanifa rejects a fixed time limit, arguing that it depends on the circumstances: what matters is whether the husband accepted congratulations or remained silent, or purchased birth tools, or let such time pass without denial. The passage is an expansion probe as it expands on the ruling with reasoning.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): The postnatal bleeding period after childbirth, typically 40 days.
نفی ولد (nafy al-walad): The husband's denial that the child is his, which if done timely leads to li'an and negation of lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Abu Hanifa says denial is never valid; Sahibayn always valid.

Key Takeaway
The timing of paternity denial in Hanafi fiqh must be prompt; the exact limit is disputed between immediate action (Abu Hanifa) and the postnatal period (Sahibayn).

Timing of Repudiating a Child: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains the conditions for valid repudiation and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on the timing of repudiating a child and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each position.

Core Idea
Repudiation of a child is valid before acceptance, not by a fixed clock.

In this passage from the Hidayah, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when can a husband validly repudiate the paternity of a newborn? Imam Abu Hanifa focuses on the husband's actions indicating acceptance, while the Sahibayn anchor validity to the nifas period. Understanding this difference is key to applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is nafy al-walad (repudiation of paternity). Its ruling is sahih (valid) if done correctly; otherwise invalid, leading to li'an and established lineage.
The text presents two criteria for validity.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa: No fixed period; validity depends on whether the husband has performed any act indicating acceptance (e.g., accepting congratulations, buying birth supplies). If no such act, repudiation is valid even after a long delay.
His proof: fixing a period is meaningless because reflection time varies; instead we look to actions that signal non-repudiation.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Repudiation is valid only during the nifas period (postpartum bleeding, typically up to 40 days). After nifas, it is invalid.
Their proof: repudiation in a short period is valid, in a long period invalid; nifas is the natural dividing line as it is a consequence of birth.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, a husband may repudiate after nifas if he has not shown acceptance. Under the Sahibayn, repudiation after nifas is invalid regardless of acceptance.
This affects whether li'an is performed or lineage is established.

Source Text

باب للعان
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم ترجمہ اور اگر مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے بچہ کے پیدا ہونے کے بعد ہی یا جس حالت میں مبارکباد قبول کی جاتی ہے یا پیدائش کی چیزیں خریدی جاتی ہیں نفی کی تو نفی کرنا صحیح ہے اور اس کی وجہ سے لعان کرے گا اور اگر اس کے بعد نفی کی تو اعان کرے گا اور نسب ثابت رہے گا اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ مدت نفاس میں نفی کرنا صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ نفی کرنا تھوڑی مدت میں صحیح ۔ ہوتا ہے اور دراز مدت میں صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ تو ہم نے ان دونوں کے درمیان مدت نفاس کو فاصل بنایا۔ کیونکہ نفاس ولادت کا اثر ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدت مقرر کرنے کے کچھ معنی نہیں اس واسطے کہ زمانہ تو غور و تامل کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور لوگوں کی حالتیں اس میں مختلف ہیں پس ہم نے ایسی چیز کا اعتبار کیا جو عدم نفی پر دلالت کرے اور وہ اس کا مبارکباد قبول کرنا یا مبارکبادی کے وقت اس کا خاموش رہنا یا اس کا سامان ولادت خرید نا۔ یا یہ وقت اس حال میں گذر گیا کہ وہ نفی کرنے سے رک گیا اور اگر شوہر غائب ہے اور اس کو ولادت کا علم نہیں ہوا پھر وہ آیا تو وہ مدت معتبر ہوگی ، جو ہم نے اصلین پر ذکر کی ہے۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں والد کی نفی کی چند صورتیں بیان کی گئیں ہیں (۱) پیدا ہوتے ہی اپنی بیوی کے بچہ کی نفی کردی (۲) اس حالت میں نفی کی جب کہ بچہ کی پیدائش پر مبارکباد قبول کی جاتی ہے (۳) اس حالت میں نفی کی جب کہ ولادت کا سامان خریدا جاتا ہے۔ ان تینوں
صورتوں میں نفی کرنا صحیح ہے۔ یعنی شوہر سے بچہ کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور اس نفی کرنے کی وجہ سے شو ہر امان کرے گا۔ اور اگر بچہ کی نفی ان اوقات کے بعد کی تو لعان کرے گا اور مرد سے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مدت نفاس کے اندر اندر بچہ کی نفی کر نا صحیح ہے۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تھوڑی مدت میں بچہ کی نفی کرنا صحیح ہے اور دراز مدت میں نفی کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے اور مدت قصیرہ اور مدت طویلہ کے درمیان فاصل مدت نفاس ہے یعنی مدت نفاس، مدت قصیرہ ہے اور اس سے زیادہ مدت طویلہ ہے اور مدت نفاس کو فاصل اس لئے قرار دیا کہ نفاس ولادت کا اثر ہے اور مبسوط میں ہے کہ مدت نفاس ولادت کی حالت کی طرح ہے یعنی اس مدت میں نہ نماز پڑھ سکتی ہے
اور نہ روزہ رکھ سکتی ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدت مقرر کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں۔ کیونکہ زمانہ تامل اور غور و خوض کیلئے ہوتا ہے اور تامل اور غور کرنے میں لوگوں کی حالتیں مختلف ہیں۔ اس لئے ہم نے ان چیزوں کا اعتبار کیا جو بچہ کی نفی نہ کرنے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں اور وہ چیزیں جو بچہ کی نفی نہ کرنے پر دلالت کرتی ہیں بچہ کی ولادت پر مبارکباد قبول کرنا یا مبارکبادی کے وقت خاموش رہنا یا ولادت کا سامان خرید نایا اتنے وقت کا ایسی حالت میں گزر جانا کہ شوہر نے بچہ کی نفی نہیں کی یہ سب باتیں اس پر دلالت کرتی ہیں کہ شو ہر بچہ کی پیدائش پر خوش ہے اور اس کو اپنا فرزند سمجھتا ہے اب اگر اس کے بعد نفی کرتا ہے تو یہ یفی کرنا درست نہیں ہو گا۔
اور اگر شوہر ولادت کے وقت موجود نہیں تھا اور اس کو ولادت کا علم بھی نہیں ہوا ۔ پھر سفر سے واپس آیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک بچہ کی نفی کرنے میں اس وقت کا اعتبار ہوگا جو اصول کے طور پر انھوں نے بیان کی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ان کے بیان کے مطابق مدت
معتبر ہوگی۔
Chapter of Li'an. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Commentary Volume 5. Translation: If a man repudiates his wife's child immediately after birth, or at a time when congratulations are accepted or birth supplies are purchased, then the repudiation is valid and due to it he will perform li'an. But if he repudiates after that, he will perform li'an and the lineage will be established. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said that repudiation during the period of nifas is valid. Their reasoning: repudiation in a short period is valid, in a long period it is not. So we made the nifas period the dividing line, because nifas is a consequence of birth. Abu Hanifa's proof: fixing a period is meaningless because the time is for reflection, and people's circumstances differ. So we considered that which indicates absence of repudiation: accepting congratulations, remaining silent at congratulations, buying birth supplies, or the time passing without repudiation. If the husband is absent and does not know of the birth, then when he returns, the period will be considered as we mentioned in the texts. Commentary: This passage explains several scenarios of repudiation by the father: (1) repudiation immediately at birth, (2) repudiation when congratulations are accepted, (3) repudiation when birth supplies are bought. In these three cases, repudiation is valid—lineage is not established and the husband does li'an. If repudiation is after these times, li'an is done and lineage is established. This is Abu Hanifa's school. The Sahibayn say repudiation during the nifas period is valid. Their proof: repudiation in a short period is valid, in a long period it is invalid. The dividing line is nifas, which is a short period and a consequence of birth. In al-Mabsut it is said that the nifas period is like the state of birth—during it, she cannot pray or fast. Abu Hanifa's proof: fixing a period has no meaning because time is for reflection and people differ. So we considered things that indicate non-repudiation, such as accepting congratulations, silence at congratulations, buying birth supplies, or the time passing without repudiation—all indicate the husband is pleased and considers the child his. After that, repudiation is not correct. If the husband was not present at birth and did not know, then when he returns from travel, the validity depends on the period as per the principle stated. According to the Sahibayn, the period is according to their statement.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of repudiating a child (nafy al-walad). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that there is no fixed period; rather, the validity of repudiation depends on whether the husband has performed any act that indicates acceptance of the child, such as accepting congratulations or buying items for the birth. If he does any such act, repudiation after that is invalid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the repudiation is valid only during the postpartum bleeding period (nifas), which they consider a short period logically separating a valid short delay from an invalid long delay. Abu Hanifa argues that a fixed period is arbitrary because the purpose of the delay is for the husband to reflect, and people's circumstances vary. Instead, the shari'ah looks to outward actions that signal acceptance or rejection. The commentary explains that if the husband repudiates immediately after birth or before showing acceptance, it is valid; after that, li'an is required and lineage is established. For an absent husband who learns later, the same principles apply based on when he becomes aware.

Key Terms
نفی ولد (nafy al-walad): Repudiation of paternity of a child by the husband, leading to li'an if done correctly.
لاعن (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery or repudiates paternity, resulting in separation.
نفاس (nifas): The period of postpartum bleeding after childbirth, typically up to 40 days.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two primary disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the time limit for valid repudiation of a child?
A) Immediately after birth only.
B) Within the nifas period.
C) Before accepting congratulations.
D) Before buying birth supplies.

Key Takeaway
The validity of repudiating a child depends on either the husband's actions indicating acceptance (Abu Hanifa) or the nifas period (Sahibayn), affecting whether li'an is required.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
7 min
The Ruling on Repudiating One Twin and Acknowledging the Other
Explains the ruling when a husband repudiates one twin but acknowledges the other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband repudiates one twin and acknowledges the other, and determine whether hadd or li'an applies.

Core Idea
Twins share one paternity; repudiating one while acknowledging the other is contradictory—both children are established as his.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a wife gives birth to twins, and the husband attempts to repudiate one but acknowledge the other. The ruling hinges on the principle that twins are created from one sperm (mā' wāḥid), so they must share the same father. The legal consequence differs based on which twin is repudiated: if the first is repudiated and the second acknowledged, the husband is liable for hadd al-qadhf; if the first is acknowledged and the second repudiated, he must perform li'an. The commentary resolves a potential objection by invoking the principle that an acknowledgment of chastity (iqrār bil-'iffa) takes precedence over a subsequent accusation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize the two cases: (1) husband repudiates first twin and acknowledges second, (2) husband acknowledges first and repudiates second.
The order of acknowledgment matters.
2
Understand the basis for paternity
The text states twins are created from one sperm (mā' wāḥid), so they share the same paternity. Therefore, repudiating one while acknowledging the other is legally contradictory.
This is qiyas jaliy based on common origin.
3
Compare the consequences
In the first scenario, the husband is liable for hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes) because his acknowledgment of the second shows his repudiation of the first was false. In the second, li'an is wajib because the repudiation is an accusation of adultery against the wife, and he did not retract.
Hadd applies when the husband belies himself; li'an when he accuses the wife.
4
Analyze the iqrār bil-'iffa principle
The commentary addresses an objection: why is it li'an and not hadd in the second scenario? Because acknowledging the first child implies the wife is chaste (iqrār bil-'iffa), and this acknowledgment takes precedence over the subsequent repudiation/accusation.
This prevents the scenario from being treated as a fresh accusation after acknowledgment of chastity.
5
Apply the rule to a similar case
Consider a husband who repudiates both twins or acknowledges both. Extend the principle to determine the ruling.
If both repudiated, li'an may apply for each; if both acknowledged, no issue.
