باب اللعان
۱۵۶
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
ایک حمل سے دو بچے جنے پہلے کی نفی کی اور دوسرے کا اعتراف کیا دونوں کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا
قال واذا ولدت ولدين فى بطن واحد فنفى الاول واعترف بالثانى يثبت نسبهما لانهما توامان خلق من ماء واحد وحد الزوج لانه اكذب نفسه بدعوى الثانى وان اعترف بالاول ونفى الثانى يثبت نسبهما لما ذكرنا ولا عن لانه قاذف بنفى الثانى ولم يرجع عنه والاقرار بالعفة سابق على القذف قصار كما اذاقال انها عفيفة ثم قال هي زانية وفى ذالك التلاعن كذاهذا
ترجمہ ... امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جب بیوی نے دو بچوں کو ایک ہی پیٹ سے جنا۔ پس شوہر نے پہلے بچہ کی نفی کی اور دوسرے بچہ کا اقرار کیا تو دونوں کا نسب اس سے ثابت ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ دونوں بچے جڑواں ہیں۔ ایک ہی منی سے پیدا ہوئے اور شوہر کو حد قذف ماری جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس نے دوسرے بچے کے نسب کا دعوی کر کے اپنے آپ کو جھوٹا بتلایا اور اگر شوہر نے پہلے بچہ کا اقرار کیا اور دوسرے بچہ کی نفی کی تو دونوں کا نسب (اس سے ) ثابت ہو جائے گا مذکورہ دلیل کی وجہ سے اور شوہر لعان کرے گا اس لئے کہ وہ دوسرے بچہ کی نفی کر کے ( بیوی کو ) تہمت لگانے والا ہے اور اپنے قول ہے رجوع بھی نہیں کیا ہے اور بیوی کے عفیفہ اور پاکدامن ہونے کا اقرار تہمت لگانے سے مقدم ہے پس گویا اس نے یوں کہا کہ یہ عفیفہ سے پھر کہا کہ یہ زانیہ ہے اور اس طرح کہنے میں با ہمی لعان کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے ایسا ہی یہاں بھی ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے ایک پیٹ سے دو بچے جنے۔ یعنی دونوں بچوں کے درمیان چھ ماہ سے کم کا فصل ہے۔ پس اس عورت کے شوہر نے پہلے بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کر دی اور دوسرے بچے کا اقرار کیا تو اس شخص سے دونوں بچوں کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دونوں بچے جڑواں ہیں ایک ہی منی سے پیدا ہوئے۔ لہذا یہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک بچہ اس کا ہو اور دوسرا اس کا نہ ہو ۔ اس واسطے دونوں بچوں کا نسب اسی سے ثابت ہوگا۔ البتہ شوہر پر حد قذف ماری جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس نے دوسرے بچہ کے نسب کا دعوی کر کے اپنے آپ کو جھوٹا بنا یا۔
اور اگر شوہر نے پہلے بچہ کے نسب کا اقرار کیا اور دوسرے بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کی تو اس صورت میں بھی دونوں بچوں کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو بھی ذکر کی ہے کہ دونوں بچے جوڑواں ہیں۔ البتہ اس صورت میں شوہر پر لعان واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں شوہر نے تہمت لگائی مگر اس سے رجوع نہیں کیا۔
والا قرار بالعفة سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ پہلے بچہ کے ثبوت نسب کا اقرار دوسرے بچہ کی نفی کرنے کے بعد بھی باقی ہے۔ پس یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ قذف کے بعد ابتداء اقرار کیا ہے اور نفی ولد اور قذف کے بعد اقرار کرنے کی صورت میں حد واجب ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا یہاں بھی حد واجب ہونی چاہیے تھی ۔ حالانکہ آپ نے لعان واجب کیا ہے۔
جواب شوہر نے پہلے بچہ کے نسب کا اقرار کر کے عورت کی عفت کا اقرار کیا ہے اور عفت کا اقرار حقیقتا قذف پر مقدم ہے اور اعتبار حقیقت کا ہوتا ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا شوہر نے کہا کہ یہ عورت عفیفہ ہے پھر کہا کہ یہ زانیہ ہے اور اس صورت میں لعان واجب ہوتا ہے
پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی لعان واجب ہو گا اس جواب کے بعد مسئلہ بے غبار ہو جائے گا اللهم اغفر لي و لكاتبه - جمیل احمد عفی عنہ ۔
Chapter of Li'an. 156. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Commentary Volume 5. A woman gave birth to two children from one pregnancy; the husband repudiated the first and acknowledged the second: both children's lineage will be established. He said: If a woman gives birth to two children in one womb, and he repudiates the first and acknowledges the second, the lineage of both is established because they are twins created from one sperm; and the husband is liable to the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) because he belied himself by claiming the second. If he acknowledges the first and repudiates the second, the lineage of both is established for the same reason, and he will perform li'an because he is an accuser by repudiating the second and did not retract. The acknowledgment of chastity is prior to the accusation, just as if he said she is chaste and then said she is an adulteress, in that case li'an is obligatory, similarly here. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: When the wife gives birth to two children from one abdomen, and the husband repudiates the first and acknowledges the second, both children's lineage is established from him because they are twins, created from one sperm. The husband will be given the hadd punishment for qadhf because he claimed the second child's lineage, thereby making himself a liar. If the husband acknowledged the first and repudiated the second, both children's lineage is established for the same reason, and the husband will perform li'an because he is an accuser by repudiating the second and did not retract. The acknowledgment of the wife's chastity is prior to the accusation; it is as if he said she is chaste then said she is an adulteress, in which case li'an is obligatory. So here also. Commentary: The issue is that a woman gave birth to two children from one abdomen, meaning the interval between them is less than six months. If the husband repudiates the first and acknowledges the second, both children's lineage is established from him because they are twins from one sperm. So how can one be his and the other not? Thus both are his. However, the husband is liable to hadd qadhf because he made himself a liar by acknowledging the second. If he acknowledges the first and repudiates the second, again both children's lineage is established for the same reason, but here li'an is wajib because the husband made an accusation (by repudiating) and did not retract. There is a question: The acknowledgment of the first child's lineage persists after repudiating the second, so it seems like a fresh acknowledgment after qadhf, which would require hadd, not li'an. The answer: The husband's acknowledgment of the first child is an acknowledgment of the wife's chastity, and that acknowledgment is prior to the accusation in reality. The reality is considered. So it is as if he said she is chaste then said she is an adulteress, in which case li'an is wajib. So here li'an is wajib. With this answer, the issue is clear. O Allah, forgive me and its writer - Jamil Ahmad, may he be pardoned.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning twin children. The matn states that if a woman gives birth to twins and the husband repudiates one but acknowledges the other, both children are established as his because twins are created from one sperm (mā' wāḥid) and thus share the same paternity. The legal consequence differs based on which twin he repudiates. If he repudiates the first and acknowledges the second, he is liable for hadd al-qadhf (prescribed punishment for false accusation) because his acknowledgment of the second shows that his repudiation of the first was false. If he acknowledges the first and repudiates the second, he must perform li'an because his repudiation is an accusation of adultery against the wife, and he has not retracted it. The commentary explains that the interval between twins is less than six months, reinforcing their common origin. It also addresses a potential objection: if the husband first acknowledges the first child (implying the wife is chaste), then repudiates the second, it seems like a fresh accusation after acknowledging chastity. However, the acknowledgment of chastity takes precedence (iqrār bil-'iffa sābiq), so the situation is treated as if he first declared her chaste and then accused her, which triggers li'an, not hadd.

Key Terms
توامان (taw'aman): Twins born from one pregnancy with an interval of less than six months.
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment of 80 lashes for falsely accusing a married person of adultery.
اقرار بالعفة (iqrar bil-'iffa): An acknowledgment that the wife is chaste, which takes precedence over a subsequent accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband repudiates his wife's firstborn twin but acknowledges the second, what is the ruling?
A) Only the acknowledged child's lineage is established.
B) Both children's lineage is established, and the husband is liable for hadd al-qadhf.
C) Both children's lineage is established, and the husband must perform li'an.
D) Neither child's lineage is established.

Key Takeaway
Twins share the same paternity; a husband cannot repudiate one while acknowledging the other, and the legal consequence (hadd vs li'an) depends on which twin he acknowledges first.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

The Meaning of 'Quru'' in the Iddah of a Free Woman (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i)
Explains iddah rulings and argues that quru' means hayd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that 'quru'' means hayd, identify the three Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi interpretation of 'quru'' as hayd is based on the plural form, the purpose of iddah, and a clarifying hadith.

The Quranic verse on iddah (2:228) instructs divorced women to wait for 'three quru''. The word 'quru'' is lexically ambiguous, meaning both menstruation and purity. This ambiguity leads to a well-known dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi argument that 'quru'' refers to menstrual periods, and the practical consequences of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the iddah of a free menstruating woman is three menstrual periods (hayd). This is derived from Q2:228 where 'quru'' is interpreted as hayd.
The Shafi'i school holds it means three purity periods (at-har).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i argument is that 'quru'' is a word of opposites, linguistically shared between hayd and tuhr, and thus the literal meaning is ambiguous.
3
Follow the Hanafi proofs
The Hanafi school provides three proofs: 1) The plural form 'aqra'' (minimum three) applies consistently only to hayd, because divorce is sunnah in a purity, making three complete purities impossible to count. 2) The purpose of iddah is to know the disassociation of the womb, which is determined by hayd, not tuhr. 3) The hadith: 'The iddah of a slave woman is two hayd' clarifies the meaning.
The first proof is nuanced; the author raises an objection about the plural sometimes meaning less than three (e.g., 'ashhur' in hajj).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i view
The Hanafis respond that even if the word is shared, the context and other evidences tip the scale towards hayd. The plural argument is supported by the hadith and the purpose.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if quru' means hayd, the iddah lasts three menstrual cycles (usually shorter); if it means at-har, the iddah lasts three complete purity periods (usually longer). This affects the woman's remarriage timing and rights.

Chapter of Iddah. Translation: This chapter is about the rulings of iddah. Explanation: Because iddah is the effect of separation and effect comes after the cause, so first the causes of separation (talaq, lian, mubarat, etc.) were mentioned; now from here the effect, i.e., the description of iddah. Lexically, iddah means a woman counting her days of menstruation. In Sharia, iddah refers to the days a woman must spend in waiting after the husband's ownership of enjoyment is removed, provided the woman was consummated with, or valid seclusion occurred, or the husband died. The cause of iddah is marriage or a doubtful marriage; its condition is the removal of marriage; its pillar is the prohibitions that were established at the time of separation; its ruling is prohibition of remarriage and other prohibitions. Based on women, there are four types of iddah: (1) three menstrual periods, (2) three months, (3) delivery, (4) four months and ten days. The first is for menstruating women, the second for non-menstruating, the third for pregnant women, and the fourth for widows. If the husband divorced his wife with a bain or raj'i divorce, or separation occurred without divorce, and she is a free woman who menstruates, her iddah is three quru'. Imam Shafi'i's view: 'And when a man divorces his wife with a bain or raj'i divorce, or separation occurs between them without divorce, and she is a free woman who menstruates, then her iddah is three quru', due to Allah's statement: And divorced women shall wait for three quru'. And if separation is without divorce, it is in the meaning of divorce, because iddah is required to determine the disassociation of the womb from pregnancy in the separation that occurs over the marriage, and this is realized in it. And al-aqru' is hayd in our view, and al-Shafi'i said: it means at-har. The word is true for both, because it is from the words of opposites, as Ibn al-Sukayt said, and it cannot include both simultaneously due to being homonymous. Carrying it to hayd is preferable: either acting on the plural form because if it is interpreted as at-har, and divorce occurs in a purity period, then it does not remain a plural; or because it indicates the disassociation of the womb, which is the objective; or due to the Prophet's saying: 'And the iddah of a slave woman is two hayd.' So this narration comes as an explanation appended to it.' Explanation: The scenario is: if a man gives his wife a bain or raj'i divorce, or separation occurs without divorce, and this woman is free and among those who menstruate, her iddah is three hayd. The author should have mentioned the condition 'wa qad dakhala biha' because iddah is obligatory on the consummated woman, not the unconsummated one, but after saying 'raj'i' this condition is no longer needed because raj'a occurs in consummated marriage, not unconsummated. And separation without divorce occurs due to option of puberty, option of emancipation, lack of compatibility, one spouse owning the other, invalid marriage, or apostasy of the wife. In all these cases, separation is without divorce. The proof that iddah is three hayd is Allah's statement. This verse is evidently about iddah of divorce, and separation without divorce is in the same ruling. Because iddah is obligatory to know the disassociation of the womb from pregnancy, and this meaning is found in separation without divorce. So separation without divorce is in the ruling of divorce. The author of Hidayah discusses the meaning of the word aqra'. He says that the word quru' is true for both hayd and tuhr, because it is from the words of opposites, and Ibn al-Sukayt said the same. And since the word is shared between two contradictory meanings, both cannot be intended simultaneously. So, in our view, quru' means hayd, and in Imam Shafi'i's view, it means tuhr. The author of Hidayah presents several proofs for his school. The first proof is that the word aqra' is mentioned in the plural form, and the minimum plural is three. So if hayd is intended, the plural is acted upon; but if tuhr is intended, acting upon the plural is impossible because the sunnah method is to give divorce during a time of purity. So there are two possibilities: either the tuhr in which divorce was given is counted in the iddah or not. If counted, three complete tuhrs will not occur; rather two complete tuhrs and a third incomplete one. If not counted, it would exceed three. In either case, the plural is not acted upon. If quru' is taken to mean hayd, then the plural is acted upon by divorcing in a tuhr and then counting three hayd after it. There is an objection to using the plural form as proof: that the plural form applies to three and also to less than three, like in 'ashhur ma'lumat' (known months) where the plural 'ashhur' is used but only two months and ten days are meant (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah). It would have been better if the author of Hidayah had used the word 'thalaathah' (three) in the verse as proof, as the author of Nur al-Anwar did. If the servant were not afraid of deviating from the text, he would mention all the wisdom that Mulla Jiwan mentioned in Tafsirat Ahmediyya while interpreting this verse. If you get a chance, do read it. The second proof is that the objective of iddah is to know the disassociation of the womb, and this objective is achieved by hayd, not by tuhr.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the meaning of 'quru'' in the Quranic verse on iddah (Q2:228). The author begins by defining iddah linguistically and technically, explaining its causes, conditions, pillars, and rulings. He then categorizes iddah into four types based on the woman's status. The specific ruling under discussion is for a free woman who menstruates: her iddah is three quru'. The text presents the Hanafi position that quru' means menstruation (hayd), and the Shafi'i position that it means purity periods (at-har). The Hanafi proof includes: (1) the plural form of aqra' (minimum three) is only consistently applicable to hayd, because if divorce is given in a purity period, counting three complete purity periods is impossible; (2) the purpose of iddah is to ensure the womb is free from pregnancy, which is determined by hayd, not by tuhr; (3) the hadith of the Prophet making the iddah of a slave woman two hayd confirms that quru' refers to hayd. The commentary raises an objection to the plural argument, noting that the plural can sometimes refer to less than three, as in the verse of hajj months (ashhur). However, the author then presents the second proof focused on the purpose of iddah. The dispute has practical implications: the Hanafi iddah of three menstrual cycles may be shorter than three purity cycles, affecting the woman's ability to remarry.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after the dissolution of marriage or death of her husband.
قروء (quru'): In this text, the Hanafi position is that it means hayd (menstrual periods); Shafi'i position is that it means at-har (purity periods).
حيض (hayd): Menstruation, the monthly discharge of blood from the uterus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does the term 'quru'' in Quran 2:228 refer to in the context of a free menstruating woman's iddah?
A) Three menstrual periods
B) Three purity periods
C) Three months
D) Delivery of a child

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the iddah of a free menstruating woman is three menstrual periods (hayd), based on the interpretation of 'quru'' as hayd.

Iddah for Free Menstruating Women: Three Menstrual Cycles with Proof
Ruling on iddah for free menstruating women with proof from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'iddah for a free menstruating divorcée and explain the Quranic proof and the analogy to separation without divorce.

Core Idea
The 'iddah of a free menstruating woman is three menstrual cycles, per Quran 2:228, extended by analogy to any separation after consummation.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling on 'iddah for free women who menstruate. Based on the clear text of Surah al-Baqarah 2:228, the Hanafi school holds that the waiting period is three menstrual cycles. We will also explore how this ruling extends to other forms of separation through legal analogy (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'iddah after divorce or separation. The ruling: it is obligatory (fard) for free menstruating women to wait three menstrual cycles.
'Iddah is a waiting period to ascertain purity of the womb.
2
Locate the primary proof
The source is Quran 2:228, which commands divorced women to wait for three quru'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form indicates obligation, and the specification of three quru' sets the duration. In Hanafi usul, quru' means menstruation.
Shafi'is interpret quru' as periods of purity (tuhr).
4
Trace the analogy for other separations
The text states that separation without divorce (e.g., khiyar, fasid nikah) is treated like divorce because the same rationale (istibra' al-rahim) applies.
The list of separations includes khiyar al-bulugh, khiyar al-'itq, lack of kafa'ah, etc.
5
Note the implicit condition of consummation
The author notes that the condition of consummation is implicit in the mention of raj'i divorce, because raj'ah only occurs after consummation. Thus, 'iddah is only required after consummation.

Source Text

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن یا طلاق رجعی دیدی ۔ یا ان دونوں میں بغیر طلاق کے فرقت واقع ہوگئی اور یہ عورت آزاد ہے اور ذوات الحیض میں سے ہے تو اس کی عدت تین حیض ہوں گے مصنف کو عبارت میں وقد دخل بہا کی قید ذکر کرنی چاہیے تھی اس لئے کہ عدت مدخول بہا پر واجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر مدخلو بہا پر مگر رجعیا کہنے کے بعد اس قید کی ضرورت نہیں رہی اس لئے کہ رجعت مدخول بہا میں ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر مدخول بہا میں اور فرقت بغیر طلاق کی صورت یہ ہے کہ خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے فرقت ہوئی یا خیار معتق کی وجہ سے یا عدم کفائت کی وجہ سے یا احد الزوجین کے آخر کا مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے یا نکاح فاسد کی وجہ سے یا عورت کے مرتدہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ان تمام صورتوں میں فرقت بغیر طلاق ہوگی۔ اس کی دلیل کہ عدت تین حیض ہوں گے باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے۔ ترجمہ یہ ہے کہ وہ عورتیں جن کو طلاق دیدی گئی وہ اپنے آپ کو تین حیض کی مدت تک روکیں۔ یہ آیت عدت طلاق میں ظاہر المراد ہے اور رہی فرقت بغیر طلاق تو یہ طلاق کے حکم میں ہے۔ کیونکہ عدت اس لئے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ تا کہ اس فرقت میں جو نکاح پر طاری ہوئی رحم کا پاک ہونا معلوم ہو جائے اور یہ معنی یعنی رحم کے پاک ہونے کو پہچاننا فرقت بغیر طلاق میں پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اس وجہ سے فرقت بغیر طلاق طلاق کے حکم میں ہوگی۔
Explanation of the ruling: If a man gives his wife a ba'in or raj'i divorce, or separation occurs without divorce (due to khiyar al-bulugh, khiyar al-‘itq, lack of kafa'ah, one spouse owning the other, fasid nikah, or the wife's apostasy), and she is free and menstruating, her 'iddah is three menstrual cycles. The author should have included the condition 'wa qad dakhala biha' because 'iddah is obligatory only after consummation. However, after mentioning raj'i divorce, this condition is unnecessary because raj'ah occurs only after consummation. Separation without divorce is treated like divorce because the purpose of 'iddah is to ascertain the purity of the womb, which also exists in such separations.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It explains the 'iddah for a free menstruating woman. The author first states that if a woman is divorced (ba'in or raj'i) or separates without divorce, her 'iddah is three menstrual cycles. He notes that the condition of consummation is implicitly covered by the mention of raj'i divorce. He then lists the various ways separation can occur without divorce. The proof is Quran 2:228, which commands divorced women to wait for three quru'. For other separations, the ruling is extended by analogy because the same rationale (istibra' al-rahim) applies.

Key Terms
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or separation before remarrying.
قروء (quru'): Plural of qur'; used in the Quran to refer to the period of 'iddah. In this passage, it is understood as menstrual cycles.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce after which the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage.

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah for a free menstruating woman after divorce or separation after consummation is three menstrual cycles, established by Quranic text and analogy.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
The Meaning of 'Quru'' in Quran 2:228: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi proofs for interpreting 'quru'' as menstruation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the meaning of 'quru'', explain the Hanafi proofs, and identify the practical difference in 'iddah calculation.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school interprets 'quru'' as menstruation, while the Shafi'i school interprets it as purity, leading to different 'iddah durations.

The term 'quru'' in Quran 2:228 is one of the most famous lexical disputes between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The correct interpretation directly affects the calculation of a woman's 'iddah after divorce. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi arguments from al-Hidayah, including linguistic analysis, the purpose of 'iddah, and a supporting hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the opposing view
Identify that the Hanafi school holds 'quru'' means menstruation (hayd), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it means purity (tuhr). Both meanings are lexically possible as the word is shared between opposites.
The word 'qur'' is from the class of words called 'addad' (antonyms).
2
Analyze the first Hanafi proof: plural form
The word 'aqra'' is plural, and the minimum of a plural (aqall al-jam') is three according to Hanafi usul. If 'quru'' means menstruation, three complete menstruations can be counted after divorce. If it means purity, counting is problematic because the purity in which divorce occurred may or may not count, leading to either two or an incomplete third purity.
Consider the objection: plural can be used for less than three (e.g., 'ashhurin ma'lumat' for two months and ten days).
3
Examine the second proof: purpose of 'iddah
The purpose of 'iddah is istibra' (ascertaining the womb is free from pregnancy), which is achieved by observing menstruation, not purity. Menstruation is a sign that the womb is not pregnant, while purity alone does not indicate this.
This is a rational argument (ma'qul).
4
Examine the third proof: hadith on slave woman
The Prophet said: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstruations.' This hadith uses 'quru'' to mean menstruation, confirming the Hanafi interpretation. The hadith explains the Quranic verse.
This is a sunnah proof (dalil naqli).
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the minimum and maximum 'iddah. Hanafi: a free woman's 'iddah ends after three menstruations (or three purifications if she does not menstruate). Shafi'i: after three pure periods (tuhr), even if she menstruates during that time.
This affects actual case rulings in divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ لفظ اقراء کی مراد پر کلام فرما رہے ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ قرو، حیض اور ظہر دونوں معنی میں حقیقت ہے کیونکہ یہ لفظ اضداد میں سے ہے امام لغت ابن السکیت کی رائے بھی یہی ہے اور چونکہ یہ لفظ دو متضاد معنی میں مشترک ہے اس لئے دونوں معنی یکبارگی مراد نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ پس لفظ قروء سے ہمارے نزدیک حیض مراد ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک طہر مراد ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اپنے مذہب کی تائید میں چند دلیلیں بیان کی ہیں۔ پہلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اقراء بصیغہ جمع مذکور ہے اور اقل جمع تین ہیں۔ پس حیض کے معنی مراد لینے کی صورت میں جمع پر عمل ہو سکتا ہے اور اگر طہر کے معنی مراد لئے جائیں تو جمع پر عمل ناممکن ہوگا۔ کیوں کہ طلاق میں مسنون طریقہ ہے کہ طہر کے زمانہ میں واقع کی جائے پس اب دو ہی صورتیں ہیں کہ وہ طہر جس میں طلاق واقع کی گئی ہے عدت میں شمار ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اگر عدت میں شمار کیا گیا تو پورے تین طہر نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ دو طہر پورے ہوں گے اور تیسر اطہر ناقص ہوگا اور اگر اس کو عدت میں شمار نہیں کیا گیا تو تین سے زائد ہو جائیں گے۔ بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں جمع پر عمل نہیں ہوا اور اگر قروء سے حیض مراد لیا گیا تو جمع پر عمل ہو جائے گا اس طرح پر کہ طہر کے زمانہ میں طلاق دے پر اس کے بعد تین حیض شمار کر لے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے صیغہ جمع سے استدلال کرنے پر اعتراض ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ صیغہ جمع کا اطلاق جس طرح تین پر ہوتا ہے تین سے کم پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے انج اشہر معلومات میں اشہر صیغہ جمع ہے۔ مگر مراد دو ماہ دس یوم ہیں۔ یعنی شوال، ذی قعدہ ، اور دس یوم ذی الحجہ کے۔ بہت مناسب ہوتا اگر صاحب ہدایہ آیت میں مذکور لفظ ثلاثہ سے استدلال کرتے ، جیسا کہ صاحب نورالانوار نے استدلال کیا ہے۔ خادم کو اگر مقصود عبارت سے ہٹ جانے کا خوف نہ ہوتا تو یہاں وہ تمام اسرار و حکم ذکر کرتا جو ملا جیون نے اس آیت کی تفسیر کرتے ہوئے تفسیرات احمدیہ میں آکر کئے ہیں۔ آپ کو موقع ہو تو ضرور مطالعہ کیجئے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عدت سے مقصود رحم کے پاک ہونے کو معلوم کرنا ہے اور یہ مقصود حیض سے حاصل ہو سکتا ہے نہ کہ طہر سے۔ تیسری دلیل حضور کا ارشاد ہے آپ نے فرمایا ہے طلاق الامة تطليقان وعدتها حيضتان ۔ پس یہ حدیث اس آیت کے لئے بیان واقع ہو جائے گی۔
The author of al-Hidayah discusses the meaning of 'quru''. He says that 'qur'' is genuine in both meanings of menstruation and purity because it is from antonyms. The linguist Ibn al-Sikkit agrees. Since the word is shared between two opposite meanings, both cannot be intended at once. Therefore, in our (Hanafi) school, 'quru'' means menstruation, while in Imam al-Shafi'i's school, it means purity. The author of al-Hidayah gives several arguments in support of his madhhab. First argument: The word 'aqra'' appears in the plural form, and the minimum of a plural is three. If the meaning of menstruation is taken, the plural can be applied; if the meaning of purity is taken, it is impossible to apply the plural. Because the sunnah method is to give divorce during a period of purity. Then there are two possibilities: whether the purity in which the divorce was given counts in the 'iddah or not. If it counts, the three pure periods are not complete; two are complete and the third is incomplete. If it does not count, there would be more than three. In both cases, the plural is not fulfilled. If 'quru'' means menstruation, the plural is fulfilled by counting three menstruations after the divorce. An objection is raised: the plural can be applied to less than three, as in 'ashhurin ma'lumat' (known months) referring to two months and ten days. The commentator notes it would have been better if the author had used the word 'thalathah' from the verse. The second argument: The purpose of 'iddah is to ascertain the purity of the womb, which is achieved by menstruation, not purity. The third argument: The Prophet said, 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstruations.' This hadith serves as an explanation of the verse.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author presents the Hanafi position that 'quru'' means menstruation, and the Shafi'i position that it means purity. He then provides three arguments: 1) Plural form necessitates three — only menstruation works because if purity were meant, the counted periods would not be complete. An objection regarding plural for less than three is mentioned. 2) The purpose of 'iddah (istibra') is achieved through menstruation. 3) The hadith about the slave woman's 'iddah being two menstruations indicates that 'quru'' in the Qur'an means menstruation.

Key Terms
قرء (qur'): A term in the Quran interpreted by Hanafis as menstruation, by Shafi'is as purity.
اقل جمع (aqall al-jam'): The minimum number for a plural is three according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does 'quru'' mean in Quran 2:228?
A) Menstrual cycles
B) Periods of purity
C) Months
D) Time periods

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'quru'' as menstruation is firmly supported by the plural form, the purpose of 'iddah, and a prophetic hadith.

Iddah for Non-Menstruating and Pregnant Women
Iddah rulings with Quranic proof for non-menstruating and pregnant women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the iddah periods for non-menstruating women and pregnant women, and cite the Quranic proof for each.

Core Idea
For non-menstruating women, iddah is three months; for pregnant women, it ends at delivery—both from the same Quranic verse.

In this lesson, we explore the rulings for two exceptional categories of women: those who do not menstruate (whether due to young age, old age, or delayed menarche) and those who are pregnant. The Quran provides clear guidance, and the Hanafi school applies it directly, with a minor internal discussion on the age of puberty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the women covered
List the three types: pre-menarche (young age), menopausal (old age), and those who reached puberty but never menstruated. Note the Hanafi discussion on puberty age: Sahibayn say 15, while Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to say 7? (unclear).
The ruling applies uniformly to all three: three months.
2
State the iddah period for each category
For non-menstruating women: three months. For pregnant women: until delivery. These are based on explicit Quranic text.
Three months stands in place of three menstrual cycles for those who do not menstruate.
3
Cite the Quranic proof
Quran 65:4: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation from among your women, if you doubt, their iddah is three months, and likewise those who have not menstruated. And those who are pregnant, their term is when they deliver their burden.'
The verse covers both rulings in one passage, making the proof explicit and certain (qat'i al-dalalah).
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
Recognize that a pregnant woman's iddah can be very short if she delivers early, or long if delivery is delayed. Three months is a fixed period for non-menstruating women, regardless of whether they might have menstruated later.
This prevents uncertainty in marital status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if she is among those who do not menstruate due to young age or old age, her 'iddah is three months, due to the saying of Allah: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation from among your women...' and similarly one who has reached the age of puberty and has not menstruated, at the end of the verse. And if she is pregnant, her 'iddah is to deliver her burden, due to the saying of Allah: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is when they deliver their burden.' Explanation: If the wife is among women who do not menstruate due to young age or old age, her 'iddah is three months. And similarly a woman who has reached puberty (according to the Sahibayn: 15 years, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa: 7 years?) but has not menstruated; her 'iddah is also three months, which stands in place of three menstruations. The proof is the verse: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation from among your women, if you have doubt, their 'iddah is three months, and likewise those who have not menstruated.' The author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that when the verse of quru' was revealed, the Companions said: We know the 'iddah of menstruating women, but we do not know the 'iddah of those who do not menstruate. So this verse was revealed to clarify that.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage provides rulings with proofs for two categories: (1) non-menstruating women (due to young age, old age, or delayed menarche) and (2) pregnant women. The 'iddah for non-menstruating women is three months, based on Quran 65:4. The 'iddah for a pregnant woman ends upon delivery, based on Quran 65:4. The commentary also mentions a background: when the verse on quru' was revealed, the Companions asked about non-menstruating women, and then the verse was revealed.

Key Terms
سن یاس (sinn al-ya's): The age of menopause, after which a woman no longer menstruates.
وضع حمل (wad' haml): Delivery of the child, which ends the 'iddah for a pregnant woman.

Checkpoint
What is the 'iddah for a divorced woman who is pregnant?
A) Three months
B) Three menstrual cycles
C) Until she delivers her child
D) One year

Key Takeaway
The Quran prescribes three months for non-menstruating women and delivery for pregnant women as the iddah period.

Slave Woman's 'Iddah and Divorce: Two Menstruations and Two Pronouncements
Ruling on slave woman's 'iddah and number of divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'iddah period and number of divorces for a slave woman, explain the principle of tansif (halving), and justify why menstruation rounds to two.

Core Idea
Slavery halves the 'iddah and divorce count, but an indivisible menstruation rounds to two.

Islamic law distinguishes between free and slave women in matters of 'iddah and divorce. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a slave woman's 'iddah is two menstrual cycles (or one and a half months if she does not menstruate) and that she is divorced by two pronouncements. We will explore the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind the halving principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are we ruling on? It is the 'iddah period and the number of divorces for a slave woman. The ruling: 'iddah = two menstruations; divorce = two pronouncements.
The act is observing 'iddah after divorce.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a hadith: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstruations.' This is an explicit textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The hadith directly states the numbers. Additionally, a rational argument is given: slavery reduces obligations by half (tansif). Since a menstruation cannot be divided into halves, the minimum becomes two.
Umar's statement illustrates the ideal would be 1.5 but menstruation prevents it.
4
Apply the exception for non-menstruating women
If the slave woman does not menstruate, her 'iddah is one and a half months. Because months are divisible, halving is directly applied: half of three months is 1.5 months.
This shows consistency: tansif works when the unit is divisible.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
While Hanafis hold two divorces, some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold three divorces for a slave woman. Both rely on different proofs.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences: after two divorces, a Hanafi slave woman is divorced; in Shafi'i, she would need a third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باندی کی عدت دو حیض اور باندی کی طلاق دو طلاقیں ہیں وان كانت امة فعدتها حيضاتان لقوله عليه السلام طلاق الامة تطليقان وعدتها حيضتان ولأن الرق منصف والحيضة لا تتجزى فكملت فصارت حیضتیان والیه اشار عمر بقوله لو استطعت لجعلنها حيضة ونصفا وان كانت لا تحيض فعدتها شهر ونصف لانه متجز فامكن تنصيفه عملا بالرق
The 'iddah of a slave woman is two menstruations, and the divorce of a slave woman is two divorces. If she is a slave, her 'iddah is two menstruations due to the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstruations.' And because slavery reduces [the number] by half, but a menstruation cannot be divided, so it is completed and becomes two menstruations. 'Umar alluded to this by saying: 'If I could, I would have made it one and a half menstruations.' And if she does not menstruate, her 'iddah is one and a half months because that is divisible, so it can be halved in accordance with slavery.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for slave women. Her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles instead of three, because slavery halves the obligations. Since menstruation cannot be halved (one cannot have half a menstruation), it is rounded up to two. If she does not menstruate, her 'iddah is one and a half months (half of three months). The proof is a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. 'Umar's statement highlights the principle: ideally it would be one and a half, but menstruation is indivisible.

Key Terms
امة (amah): A female slave.
تنصيف (tansif): Halving; the principle that slave women's obligations are halved compared to free women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Three months

Key Takeaway
A slave woman's 'iddah is two menstruations (or 1.5 months if not menstruating) and she is divorced by two pronouncements, due to the principle of tansif (halving) from slavery.

Iddah of Free Women Who Do Not Menstruate
Ruling on 'iddah of free non-menstruating women with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'iddah duration for a free woman who does not menstruate, identify the Quranic proof, and distinguish the three scenarios to which this ruling applies.

Core Idea
For a free woman who does not menstruate, the 'iddah is three months, established by explicit Quranic text.

This lesson examines the 'iddah of women who do not experience menstruation, whether due to youth, menopause, or delayed menstruation after puberty. The Hanafi school derives the ruling directly from Surah al-Talaq (65:4), which specifies a three-month waiting period. We will explore the three scenarios covered by this ruling and the Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the 'iddah (waiting period) of a free woman who does not menstruate. The ruling is that her 'iddah is three months (wajib).
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The proof is Surah al-Talaq (65:4), which explicitly states the three-month 'iddah for women who have despaired of menstruation and those who have not yet menstruated.
The verse is the primary textual evidence.
3
Understand the occasion of revelation (sabab al-nuzul)
According to Fath al-Qadir, when the verse on 'iddah for menstruating women was revealed, the Companions asked about non-menstruating women, and then this verse was revealed to answer their question.
4
Distinguish the three scenarios
The ruling applies to: (1) young girls before puberty, (2) menopausal women, and (3) women who have reached the age of majority but have not yet menstruated. All have the same three-month 'iddah.
The three months substitute for three menstrual cycles.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on age of majority
Imam Abu Hanifa considers the age of majority as 17 years, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it 15 years. This difference does not affect the 'iddah ruling; all agree that a woman who has not menstruated after reaching the age of majority has an 'iddah of three months.

ترجمہ اور اگر بیوی ان عورتوں میں سے ہے جن کو صغر سنی یا بڑھاپے کی وجہ سے حیض نہیں آتا ہے تو اس کی عدت تین ماہ ہے باری تعالیٰ کے قول واللائی یسن الآیۃ کی وجہ سے۔ یعنی وہ عورتیں جو حیض سے مایوس ہو گئیں ( ان کی عدت تین ماہ ہیں اور ایسے ہی وہ عورت جو عمر کے لحاظ سے بالغہ ہو گئی اور اس کو حیض نہیں آتا تو اس کی عدت بھی تین ماہ ہے ) دلیل اس آیت کا آخر ہے

تشریح اس عبارت میں غیر ذوات الحیض کی چند صورتیں بیان کی ہیں ایک تو یہ کی حیض کا نہ آنا صغرسنی کی وجہ سے ہے، دوم یہ کہ عورت سن یاس (بڑھاپے کو پہنچ گئی ہے، اس لئے حیض نہیں آتا ، سوم یہ کہ عورت عمر کے لحاظ سے بالغہ ہوگئی صاحبین کے نزدیک پندرہ سال کی ہو گئی اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک ۷ ارسال ہوگئی ۔ مگر ابھی تک حیض نہیں آیا ان تینوں قسم کی عورتوں کی عدت تین ماہ ہوگئی ۔ جو تین حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ واللائي يحسن من المحيض من نسائكم ان ارتبم فعد تهن ثلاثة اشهر واللائى لم يحضن یعنی تمھاری (مطلقہ ) بیویوں میں سے جو عورتیں (بوجہ زیادت سن کے ) حیض آنے سے مایوس ہو چکی ہیں۔ اگر تمھیں ( ان کی عدت کی تعین میں ) شبہ ہو تو ان کی عدت تین ماہ ہیں اور اسی طرح جن عورتوں کو اب تک بوجہ کم عمری کے ) حیض نہیں آیا۔ (مرشد تھا نوئی) صاحب فتح القدیر نے لکھا ہے کہ جب آیت قروء نازل ہوئی تو صحابہ نے کہا کہ ذوات الحیض کی عدت تو ہمیں معلوم ہوگئی مگر جن عورتوں کو حیض نہیں آیا ان کی عدت کا ابھی تک علم نہیں ہو سکا تو اس پر یہ آیت نازل ہوئی۔ یعنی اگر تم کو غیر ذوات الحیض کی عدت میں شبہ ہے اور ابھی تک علم نہیں ہو سکا تو سنو ان کی عدت تین ماہ ہے۔
And if she is among those who do not menstruate due to youth or old age, her 'iddah is three months, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who despair of menstruation among your women...' the verse, and likewise the one who has reached the age of maturity and has not menstruated, at the end of the verse.

Translation: And if the wife is among those women who do not menstruate due to young age or old age, her 'iddah is three months, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who despair of menstruation...' the verse. That is, women who have despaired of menstruation (their 'iddah is three months), and likewise the woman who has reached the age of maturity and does not menstruate, her 'iddah is also three months. The evidence is the end of this verse.

Commentary: In this passage, several cases of non-menstruating women are mentioned. First, that menstruation does not occur due to young age. Second, that the woman has reached the age of menopause (old age), therefore menstruation does not occur. Third, that the woman has reached the age of maturity according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) she has reached fifteen years, and according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) she has reached seventeen years, but still has not menstruated. For all three types of women, the 'iddah is three months, which stands in place of three menstruations. The evidence is this verse: 'And those who despair of menstruation among your women, if you are in doubt, their 'iddah is three months, and also those who have not menstruated.' That is, among your (divorced) wives, the women who have despaired of menstruation (due to advanced age), if you are in doubt (about the determination of their 'iddah), their 'iddah is three months, and similarly the women who have not yet menstruated (due to young age). (Murshid Thanawi) The author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that when the verse of 'quru' was revealed, the Companions said: 'We know the 'iddah of menstruating women, but we have not yet known the 'iddah of those who do not menstruate.' Then this verse was revealed: 'If you are in doubt about the 'iddah of non-menstruating women and have not yet known, then listen: their 'iddah is three months.'
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Hidayah on the 'iddah of free women who do not menstruate. The matn states that the 'iddah for such women is three months, citing the Quranic verse from Surah al-Talaq. The commentary (Ashraf al-Hidayah) expands by clarifying three scenarios: (1) young girls who have not yet begun menstruating, (2) menopausal women, and (3) women who have reached the age of maturity (15 by the Sahibayn, 17 by Imam Abu Hanifa) but have not yet menstruated. The commentary also relates the occasion of revelation: when the verse on menstrual 'iddah was revealed, the Companions asked about those who do not menstruate, and then the verse with the three-month ruling was revealed. The 'iddah of three months substitutes for three menstrual cycles, as the Quran specifies this for non-menstruating women. The Hanafi position is that this ruling applies to all free women who do not menstruate, regardless of the reason. The intra-Hanafi difference on the age of majority (15 vs 17) is noted but does not affect the 'iddah ruling.

Key Terms
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.
ذوات الحیض (dhawat al-hayd): Women who menstruate regularly.
صغر (sughr): Young age, i.e., before the age of puberty.
كبر (kibar): Old age, specifically menopause (sin al-yas).

Iddah of a Pregnant Woman Until Delivery
Ruling on 'iddah of a pregnant woman ending with delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'iddah of a pregnant woman, cite the Qur'anic proof, and explain why the 'iddah ends with delivery.

Core Idea
The 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends with delivery, regardless of the time elapsed.

This lesson addresses a clear and unambiguous ruling from the Qur'an: the waiting period ('iddah) of a pregnant woman, whether divorced or widowed, terminates upon delivery of her child. The proof is the verse from Surah al-Talaq (65:4), which leaves no room for alternative interpretation. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary hardship and ensures compliance with the divine command.

Guided Path
1
State the Rule
The 'iddah of a pregnant woman (whether divorced or widowed) ends when she delivers her child.
This is the ruling from the matn of Hidayah.
2
Cite the Proof
Recite or reference Qur'an 65:4: 'And those with pregnancy, their term is that they deliver their pregnancy.'
The verse is directly quoted in the source.
3
Explain the Proof
The word 'ajal (term) refers to the 'iddah period, and 'an yada'na' (that they deliver) explicitly sets delivery as the endpoint. The text is clear (qati al-dalala).
No need for further interpretation; the ruling is direct.
4
Note the Scope
This ruling applies equally to divorced and widowed pregnant women. The verse does not distinguish.
The same verse is cited for both cases.
5
Confirm the Consensus
All schools of fiqh agree on this ruling; there is no ikhtilaf (valid disagreement).
The cross_madhhab_status is muttafaq alayh.

The proof is the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Talaq (65:4). The commentary translates and notes the evidence. Note: This applies regardless of the time elapsed; even if delivery occurs immediately after the divorce, the 'iddah ends. The Hanafi position is unanimous on this. Iddah of a Divorced Slave Woman
Ruling on 'iddah of a divorced slave woman with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the 'iddah duration for a divorced slave woman in both menstruating and non-menstruating cases, and EXPLAIN the rational principle (munassif) that leads to the halving.

Core Idea
Slavery halves the 'iddah: a menstruating slave waits two cycles; a non-menstruating slave waits one and a half months.

We have previously learned about the 'iddah of free women. Now we turn to the 'iddah of slave women, which is reduced due to the legal status of slavery (riqq). This passage from al-Hidayah presents the ruling for both menstrual and non-menstrual cases, supported by a hadith and a rational principle that slavery halves many legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage distinguishes between a divorced slave woman who menstruates and one who does not. Each has a different 'iddah duration.
2
State the ruling for each case
For the menstruating slave woman, the 'iddah is two menstrual cycles. For the non-menstruating slave woman, the 'iddah is one and a half months.
Compare with free woman: three cycles / three months.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles.' This is a direct textual proof for the menstruating case.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the Hanafi school accepts it for establishing rulings.
4
Understand the rational principle (munassif)
Slavery halves rulings. Since a menstrual cycle cannot be halved, it is rounded up to two full cycles. Months, however, can be halved, so the non-menstruating case is exactly half of the free woman's three months.
This principle is consistent with other halving rules, e.g., hudud punishments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ مملوک ہونا نعمت اور عذاب کو آدھا کرنے والا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد فعلیھن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب اور ایک حیض متجری نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے وہ پورا ہو گیا تو اس طرح باندی مطلقہ کی عدت دو حیض ہوں گے اور اس کی طرف حضرت عمر نے اشارہ فرمایا کہ اگر میرے بس میں ہوتا تو میں مطلقہ باندی کی عدت ڈیڑھ حیض کر دیتا۔ مگر چونکہ یہ بات میرے بس میں نہیں اس لئے میں نے اس کو پورے دو حیض کر دیا اور اگر وہ مطلقہ باندی غیر ذوات الحیض میں سے ہو تو اس کی عدت ڈیڑھ ماہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ مہینہ متجری (ٹکڑے) ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس رقیت پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس کی تنصیف کر دی جائے گی۔
And if she is a slave woman, her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles.' And because slavery halves (benefits and punishments), and a single menstrual cycle cannot be divided, so it is completed, thus it becomes two menstrual cycles. And Umar alluded to this by saying: 'If I could, I would make it one and a half cycles.' And if she does not menstruate, her 'iddah is one and a half months, because a month can be divided, so it is possible to halve it in accordance with slavery.

Translation: And if this woman is a slave, her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles.' And because being owned halves (blessings), and a single menstrual cycle cannot be halved, so it is completed, thus it became two cycles. And Umar alluded to this by saying: 'If I could, I would make her 'iddah one and a half cycles.' And if the slave woman is such that she does not menstruate, her 'iddah is one and a half months, because a month can be divided, so it is possible to halve it by acting upon slavery.

Commentary: The ruling is that if a divorced slave woman, her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles.' And the rational proof is that being owned halves (blessings and punishments). Thus, the command: 'So for them is half of what is upon the free women from punishment.' A single menstrual cycle cannot be divided, so it is completed, and thus the 'iddah of a divorced slave woman becomes two cycles. Umar alluded to this: 'If I could, I would make the 'iddah of a divorced slave woman one and a half cycles.' But since I cannot, I made it two full cycles. And if the divorced slave woman is among non-menstruating women, her 'iddah is one and a half months, because a month can be divided (into halves). So acting upon slavery, it is halved.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage addresses the 'iddah of a divorced slave woman (amah). The matn from Hidayah states two rulings: if she menstruates, her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles; if she does not menstruate, it is one and a half months. The proof is a hadith: 'The divorce of a slave woman is two divorces, and her 'iddah is two menstrual cycles.' The commentary explains the rational basis: slavery halves everything (e.g., punishment for zinā is half). Since a menstrual cycle cannot be halved, it is rounded up to two complete cycles. Umar's statement illustrates that ideally it would be 1.5 cycles, but since that is impossible, it is set at two. For non-menstruating slave women, months can be halved, so the 'iddah is one and a half months (half of three months for a free woman). The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
امة (amah): A female slave (bondwoman).
رق (riqq): Slavery; the state of being owned.
منصف (munassif): Halving; the principle that slavery reduces rulings by half.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the 'iddah of a divorced slave woman who does not menstruate?
A) Three months
B) Two months
C) One and a half months
D) One month

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah of a slave woman is reduced by half due to slavery: two cycles for menstruating, one and a half months for non-menstruating.

Iddah of a Widow: Free and Slave Women
Ruling on 'iddah of a widow with Quranic proof and a note on historical ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'iddah duration for free and slave widows, cite the Quranic evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the alternative view of a one-year 'iddah.

Core Idea
A widow's 'iddah is fixed: four months ten days for free women, halved for slaves—no alternative.

The 'iddah of a widow is one of the most clearly defined waiting periods in Islamic law, based directly on a Quranic verse. This passage from the Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling for free and slave widows, emphasizing that the obligation applies universally regardless of age, faith, or consummation. It also mentions an early disagreement about a potential one-year 'iddah, which the Hanafi school decisively rejects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
First, note that the passage gives the 'iddah for a free widow (four months ten days) and for a slave widow (two months five days). Observe that the ruling applies to all free widows without exception, as the commentary expands.
The universality includes non-Muslim widows, minors, and non-consummated marriages.
2
Locate the primary proof
The ruling is explicitly based on Quran 2:234, which commands widows to wait four months and ten days. Identify that this is a clear, unambiguous text (qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah) and the imperative indicates obligation (wujub).
No other verse overrides this for widows, though pregnancy changes the end date.
3
Understand the halving principle for slaves
The slave's 'iddah is exactly half (two months five days) because the text states 'because slavery halves.' This is a Hanafi principle: obligations on slaves are halved unless the text specifies otherwise.
Compare with the free widow's period: 4 months 10 days = 130 days; half = 65 days = 2 months 5 days.
4
Analyze the historical ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that some early jurists held that a widow has two options: a one-year 'iddah (azimah) or four months ten days (rukhsah). Identify that the Hanafi school rejects the one-year view, considering the Quranic duration as the sole obligation.
This ikhtilaf is noted but not adopted; the mufta bihi is the shorter period.
5
Distill the ruling anatomy
Extract the essential components: the act (observing 'iddah) is wajib, the duration is fixed, and no external conditions (except pregnancy) alter it. The ruling applies to all widows regardless of personal circumstances.
This is a pure obligation with no room for concession or choice.

And the 'iddah of a free woman in the case of death is four months and ten days, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days.' And the 'iddah of a slave woman is two months and five days, because slavery halves.

Translation: And the 'iddah of a free woman whose husband has died is four months and ten days. Because the command of Allah Most High: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days.' And the 'iddah of a slave woman (whose husband has died) is two months and five days, because being owned halves.

Commentary: The ruling is that the 'iddah of a free woman whose husband has died is four months and ten days, whether this woman is menstruating or not, Muslim or People of the Book, adult or minor, consummated or not, menopausal or not, and whether her husband was free or slave.

The evidence is the saying of Allah, the Lord of Honor: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days.' And if the woman whose husband died is a slave, her 'iddah is two months and five days, because slavery halves.

Benefits: There is a difference among the early jurists regarding the 'iddah of a woman whose husband has died. Some say that she has two 'iddahs: a long 'iddah of one year and a short 'iddah of four months and ten days. So observing the 'iddah for one year is azimah (strict adherence) and four months and ten days is rukhsah (concession).

Commentary
This passage from Hidayah deals with the 'iddah of a widow. The matn states that a free woman whose husband dies must observe 'iddah for four months and ten days, quoting the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:234). A slave widow's 'iddah is two months and five days, due to the principle of halving (slavery halves). The commentary emphasizes that this ruling applies universally to all free widows regardless of age, faith, consummation, etc. It also mentions an ikhtilaf among early jurists: some hold that a widow has two options for 'iddah: one year (azimah) or four months and ten days (rukhsah). However, the Hanafi school, as per the matn, adopts the shorter period as the sole obligation. This difference is noted but not adopted. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

A free widow waits four months and ten days; a slave widow waits half that.

This lesson addresses the waiting period ('iddah) for widows, a wajib obligation following the death of a husband. The ruling is directly rooted in the Quran for free women, and the principle of slavery halving obligations extends it to slave women. We will examine the text and its proof.

Widow's 'Iddah: One Year or Four Months Ten Days?
Dispute about widow's 'iddah length

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a widow's 'iddah is only four months and ten days and evaluate the minority view that allows a one-year option as a concession.

Core Idea
A widow's 'iddah is only four months and ten days; the earlier one-year ruling was abrogated.

This passage addresses a difference among early scholars regarding the length of a widow's 'iddah. Some held that the original obligation was one year, with four months and ten days as a concession, while the majority (including the Hanafi school) maintained that the one-year ruling was abrogated by a later Quranic verse. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Quranic text is interpreted and how abrogation (naskh) operates in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting opinions
Read the passage and note that some early scholars propose two 'iddahs: a full year as azima and four months ten days as rukhsa. The majority (Hanafi) say only four months ten days remains because the earlier one-year verse was abrogated.
2
Analyze the evidence for each opinion
The minority cites Quran 2:240 (provision for one year) as proof of the one-year 'iddah, with 2:234 (four months ten days) as a concession. The majority cites 2:234 as the final, abrogating verse.
Identify the two verses: 2:240 and 2:234.
3
Understand the concept of naskh (abrogation)
Abrogation means a later divine ruling supersedes an earlier one. In Hanafi usul, naskh is accepted when the abrogating text is dated later. Here, 2:234 (from the later Medinan period) abrogates 2:240 (from earlier).
Naskh removes the original ruling entirely; it does not leave a choice.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
After presenting both views, the text concludes with 'Wallahu a'lam bi as-sawab', indicating that the abrogation view is correct. Thus, the operative ruling is that a widow's 'iddah is four months and ten days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Benefits: There is a difference among the early jurists regarding the 'iddah of a woman whose husband has died. So some hold the opinion that the 'iddah of such a woman is two: the long 'iddah is one year, and the short 'iddah is four months and ten days. So observing 'iddah for one year is azima, and four months and ten days is rukhsa. They derive evidence from the saying of Allah: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, (let them make) a bequest for their wives, provision for one year, without turning them out. But if they go out, there is no sin on you for what they do with themselves in a reasonable manner.' That is, those who die among you and leave wives, they should make a bequest for their wives for one year's maintenance, on the condition that they are not expelled from the house. However, if they leave on their own, there is no sin on you regarding what they do with themselves in a reasonable manner. These scholars argue from this verse that the 'iddah of a widow is one year, but if they leave after four months and ten days and end the 'iddah, there is no harm. So the point is that the full 'iddah is one year, but acting upon four months and ten days is a concession. And the general opinion of the people of knowledge is that at the beginning of Islam, the 'iddah of a widow was one year, as mentioned in this verse. But later the ruling was abrogated due to the verse 'yatarabbasna bi anfusihinna arba'ata ashhurin wa 'ashran' and the 'iddah of the widow became fixed at four months and ten days. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute among early fuqaha regarding the 'iddah of a widow. Some scholars held that the widow's 'iddah is actually one year (azima - the original obligation), but a concession (rukhsa) allows it to be just four months and ten days. Their proof is the Quranic verse about bequest for one year (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:240). They interpret this verse as establishing a one-year 'iddah, with the possibility of ending it earlier as a concession. However, the majority of scholars (jomhur) hold that this initial ruling was abrogated (mansukh) by the subsequent verse (2:234) which specifies four months and ten days. The phrase 'yatarabbasna bi anfusihinna arba'ata ashhurin wa 'ashran' is considered the final ruling. The text endorses the view of abrogation, as indicated by 'Wallahu a'lam bi as-sawab'. This is the Hanafi position and the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azima): The original, more rigorous obligation; the stricter ruling without concession.
رخصت (rukhsa): A concession or leniency that lightens the original obligation under certain circumstances.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a previous ruling replaced by a later one from Quran or Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the widow's 'iddah regarding the one-year ruling?
A) One year is the azima and four months ten days is rukhsa, both valid.
B) The one-year ruling was abrogated and only four months ten days remains.
C) Neither, it is two months five days.
D) The widow chooses whichever she prefers.

Key Takeaway
For a widow, the operative Hanafi ruling is that her 'iddah is fixed at four months and ten days; the earlier one-year provision is abrogated and no longer applicable.

The 'Iddah of a Pregnant Woman Ends with Delivery
Ruling on 'iddah of a pregnant woman with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'iddah of a pregnant woman, cite the primary Quranic proof, and explain why a pregnant widow's 'iddah ends with delivery even if it occurs before four months and ten days.

Core Idea
The 'iddah of any pregnant woman ends with delivery — the Quranic verse governs absolutely.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we learn a crucial rule: the waiting period ('iddah) of a pregnant woman terminates immediately upon delivery. This applies regardless of whether she was divorced or widowed. The primary evidence is the clear Quranic verse from Surah At-Talaq. The passage also resolves an apparent conflict with the verse for widows, establishing that the pregnancy verse takes precedence through abrogation or specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the 'iddah of a pregnant woman. The ruling is that it ends with delivery (wad' al-haml). Note that this applies whether the separation was by divorce or death.
This is a clear statement of the Hanafi position.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (Surah At-Talaq 65:4): 'Wa ulaatu al-ahmali ajaluhunna an yada'na hamlahunna' (And for those who are pregnant, their term is until they deliver their child).
This is a text with qat'i thubut (certain transmission) and qat'i dalalah (clear meaning).
3
Analyse the dalil: mutlaq and generality
The verse is mutlaq (absolute/unqualified) – it does not specify whether the pregnancy is from divorce or death. In Hanafi usul, a mutlaq text applies to all its instances unless a specific restriction (takhsis) is proven. Thus, the ruling covers both divorced and widowed pregnant women.
The key term 'ajaluhunna' indicates the end of the 'iddah.
4
Address the apparent conflict with the widow's verse
Surah Al-Baqarah (2:234) prescribes four months and ten days for widows. However, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) reports that the pregnancy verse (Surah At-Talaq) was revealed later, effectively abrogating or specifying the earlier verse for pregnant widows. Umar (RA) and Shuraih (RA) confirm this ruling.
This resolves the potential contradiction: the later revelation takes precedence.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے ان كانت حاملا فعدتها ان تضع حملها لاطلاق قوله تعالى واولات الاحمال اجلهن ان يضعن حملهن قال عبدالله ابن مسعود من شاء باهلته ان سورة النساء القصرى نزلت بعد الآية التي في سورة البقرة وقال عمر لو وضعت وزحها على سريرة لانقضت عدتها وحل لها ان تتزوج رجمہ اور اگر متوفی عنہا ز و جہا حاملہ ہے تو اس کی عدت یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے حمل کو جن دے۔ اسلئے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول و اولات لاحمال اجلهن ان يضعن حملهن مطلق ہے اور عبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص چاہے میں اس سے مباہلہ کر سکتا ہوں کہ سورہ نساء قصری (سورۃ طلاق پارہ (۲۸) اس آیت کے بعد نازل ہوئی جو سورہ بقرہ میں ہے اور حضرت عمرؓ نے کہا کہ اگر عورت نے اسی حالت میں وضع حمل کیا کہ اس کا شوہر تختہ میت پر ہے تو بھی اس کی عدت گزر گئی اور اس عورت کیلئے سحلال ہو گیا کہ ( دوسرے شوہر ) سے کاح کرلے۔ شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ متوفی عنہا ز و جہا آزاد ہو یا باندی اگر حاملہ ہو تو اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول اولات الاحمال اجـلـهـن ان يضعن حملهن مطلق ہے۔ پس اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے متوفی عنہاز و جہا اور غیر متوفی عنہا ز و جہا ب کو شامل ہے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن مسعود فر ماتے ہیں کہ سورہ بقرہ کی آيت يتربصن بانفسهن اربعة اشهر و عشراً پہلے نازل ہوئی اور سورہ نساء مری یعنی سورہ طلاق کی آیت و اولات الاحمال اجلهن ان يضعن جملهن بعد ميں نازل ہوئی ہے اور اگر کوئی اس پر مباہلہ کرنا
The 'iddah of a pregnant woman is until she delivers her child. If she is pregnant, her 'iddah is that she delivers her pregnancy, due to the unqualified statement of Allah: 'And for those who are pregnant, their term is until they deliver their child.' Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: Whoever wishes, I can take an oath [Mubahala] that Surah an-Nisa' al-Qusra (Surah at-Talaq) was revealed after the verse in Surah al-Baqarah. And Umar said: If a woman delivers while her husband is on his bier, her 'iddah has expired and it becomes lawful for her to marry. Shuraih said: The woman whose husband has died, whether free or slave, if she is pregnant, her 'iddah is until delivery. The proof is that Allah's statement 'Wa ulaatu al-ahmali ajaluhunna an yada'na hamlahunna' is general. So due to its generality, it includes the widow and the divorced woman. And Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: The verse in Surah al-Baqarah 'yatarabbasna bi anfusihinna arba'ata ashhurin wa 'ashran' was revealed earlier, and the verse of Surah an-Nisa' as-Sughra (i.e., Surah at-Talaq) 'wa ulaatu al-ahmali ajaluhunna an yada'na hamlahunna' was revealed later, and if anyone wishes to contest, [let them].
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage establishes the rule that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends with delivery, regardless of whether she was divorced or widowed. The primary proof is the Quranic verse from Surah at-Talaq (65:4): 'And for those who are pregnant, their term is until they deliver their child.' The verse is general ('amm) and includes both divorced and widowed women. The passage also emphasizes that this ruling applies absolutely, even if the delivery occurs immediately after the husband's death, as indicated by the statement of Umar. The text also addresses a potential conflict: there is a separate verse (2:234) that specifies four months and ten days for widows. How do these apply to a pregnant widow? The answer is presented through the statement of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the verse about pregnant women (Surah at-Talaq) was revealed after the verse about the four months and ten days, implying that the pregnancy verse abrogates or specifies the general widow verse. Therefore, a pregnant widow's 'iddah ends with delivery, even if it is before four months and ten days. The text also mentions Shuraih's statement applying the rule equally to free and slave women. The ruling is clear: the later revelation (Surah at-Talaq) takes precedence, making delivery the only criterion for pregnant women.

Key Terms
وضع حمل (wad' al-haml): Delivery of the child; giving birth.
مطلق (mutlaq): Unqualified, general, absolute.

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah of any pregnant woman, whether divorced or widowed, ends with the delivery of her child, based on the absolute Quranic verse in Surah At-Talaq.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Iddah of a Woman Divorced During Husband's Terminal Illness
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on iddah length when divorce and widowhood coincide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the iddah of a woman divorced ba'in during her husband's terminal illness and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When divorce and widowhood coincide, the iddah is the longer term, combining both obligations.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a husband divorces his wife irrevocably (ba'in) during a terminal illness, then dies within the iddah. The wife inherits from him due to the Companions' consensus on the 'woman of Far' case. The key question: what is her iddah? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf. Understanding the reasoning behind each view and the practical consequences is essential for correctly applying the iddah rules in such overlapping cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling type
Recognize the specific case: a ba'in divorce (irrevocable) issued during the husband's terminal illness, followed by his death within the iddah. The wife inherits. This triggers a dispute over the iddah length.
The ruling for raj'i divorce is different; by consensus, the iddah of death applies.
2
State each opinion
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: iddah is the longer of three menstruations or four months ten days (ab'ad al-ajalayn). Abu Yusuf: iddah is only three menstruations.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Yusuf argues the marriage was severed by divorce before death, so only divorce iddah applies; inheritance survives but does not affect iddah. The majority argue that since the marriage is deemed to continue for inheritance (by ijma), it should also continue for iddah as a precaution (ihtiyat), thus combining both terms.
The majority rely on qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) and the principle of precaution.
4
Recognize the practical difference
Under the majority, the woman must wait until the longer term expires. For example, if three menstruations finish before four months ten days, she waits until four months ten days. If four months pass without three menstruations (e.g., extended purity), she waits until three menstruations occur. Under Abu Yusuf, she only waits three menstruations regardless.
The difference can be years if the woman has infrequent menstruation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the longer term). This is supported by the majority and the principle of ihtiyat.
Refer to al-Hidayah and later fatwa collections.

Source Text
