The 'Iddah of a Slave-Wife Purchased by Her Husband: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah for a slave-wife purchased and freed by her husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the 'iddah of a woman bought by her husband and freed, and identify the practical difference between these views.

Core Idea
Ownership blocks 'iddah; upon manumission, 'iddah revives, but scholars differ on how many periods.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a complex scenario: a man purchases his own wife who is a slave. The marriage becomes corrupt, but the wife is now his property. What 'iddah rulings apply? The passage details the views of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Imam Zufar. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to how ownership and possession affect 'iddah obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal situation
The husband buys his own slave-wife. The marriage becomes fasid. She is now owned by him, so milk yamin prevents 'iddah.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling
When he frees her, she must observe two hayd for the fasid marriage (with mourning) and one hayd for manumission (without mourning).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's counter-argument
They consider the woman still under the first marriage's possession; the renewal of marriage during 'iddah makes the second marriage as if consummated, requiring full mahr and a separate full 'iddah.
4
Note Imam Zufar's view
He argues the first 'iddah falls away (al-saqit la ya'ud) and the second divorce is before consummation, so no 'iddah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: number of hayd and whether a full 'iddah is required after the second marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب اس شخص نے اپنی منکوحہ باندی کو خریدا تو نکاح فاسد ہو گیا اور اس باندی پر دو حیض بطور عدت واجب ہو گئے۔ چنانچہ اس باندی کا نکاح کسی دوسرے سے جائز نہیں تا وقتیکہ عدت کا زمانہ گذر جائے۔ مگر خود اس کے حق میں عدت کا حکم ظاہر نہیں ہوا کیونکہ مانع عدت یعنی ملک یمین موجود ہے پس جب اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو مانع عدت زائل ہو گیا اس وجہ سے اب خود اس کے حق میں بھی عدت کا حکم ظاہر ہوگا، لہذا دو حیض بطور عدت کے فساد نکاح کی وجہ سے واجب ہوں گے اور اس میں اس کو سوگ منانالازم ہوگا اور تیسرا حیض آزاد ہونے کیوجہ سے واجب ہوگا اور اس میں سوگ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عورت در حقیقت پہلی ولی کیوجہ سے اپنے شوہر کے ہاتھ میں مقبوضہ ہے اور ابھی تک ولی اولی کا اثر یعنی عدت بھی باقی ہے پس جب شوہر نے عدت کے زمانہ میں تجدید نکاح کیا در انحالیکہ وہ عورت نکاح اول میں دخول کی وجہ سے مقبوضہ ہے تو وہ قبضہ جو نکاح اول میں دخول کی وجہ سے تھا اس دوسرے نکاح کے قبضہ واجبہ کے قائم مقام ہو جائے گا۔ پس جب اس کو طلاق دی تو ایسا ہو گیا گویا اس نے اس کو نکاح ثانی میں بھی دخول کے بعد طلاق دی ہے اس وجہ سے شوہر پر پورا مہر اور عورت پر مستقلاً دوسری عدت واجب ہوگی اور اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ غاصب نے مالک سے اس شئی مغصوب کو خریدا جو غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہے تو اس صورت میں غاصب محض عقد بیع کی وجہ سے قبضہ کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ کسی جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ جو قبضہ حالت غصب میں ہی اس قبضہ کے قائم مقام ہو گیا جو بیع کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ نکاح ثانی کے بعد طلاق بعد الدخول ہے نہ قبل الدخول۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح ثانی کی وجہ سے عدت اولی ساقط ہو گئی ہے لہذاوہ لوٹ کر نہیں آئے گی۔ اس لئے کہ قاعدہ ہے الساقط لا یعود اور عدت ثانیہ واجب نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ نکاح ثانی کے بعد طلاق قبل الدخول واقع ہوئی ہے اور طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب سابق میں گذر چکا، ملاحظہ فرمالیا جائے۔
For when this person purchased his own married slave-woman, the marriage became corrupt (fasid), and two menstrual periods became obligatory as 'iddah upon this slave-woman. So her marriage to someone else is not permissible until the period of 'iddah passes. However, with respect to himself, the ruling of 'iddah did not become apparent because the impediment to 'iddah, i.e., ownership by right of the right hand (milk yamin), existed. Then when he freed her, the impediment to 'iddah was removed, so now with respect to himself also the ruling of 'iddah will become apparent. Therefore, two menstrual periods will be obligatory as 'iddah due to the corrupt marriage, and in that period she must observe mourning (sog), and a third menstrual period will be obligatory due to manumission, and in that mourning is not necessary. The proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that this woman is in reality in the possession of her husband due to the first marriage, and the effect of the first marriage, i.e., 'iddah, still remains. So when the husband renewed the marriage during the 'iddah period, while the woman is possessed due to consummation in the first marriage, that possession which was due to consummation in the first marriage will stand in place of the possession obligatory due to this second marriage. So when he divorced her, it became as if he divorced her after consummation in the second marriage. Therefore, the full mahr is obligatory upon the husband, and a separate second 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman. An analogy for this is when a usurper purchases the usurped object from its owner while it is in the usurper's possession, then in this case the usurper becomes a possessor merely by the contract of sale; no new possession is needed because the possession that existed in the state of usurpation stands in place of the possession that becomes obligatory due to sale. So it is proven that the divorce after the second marriage is after consummation, not before. Imam Zufar's proof is that due to the second marriage, the first 'iddah has fallen away, so it will not return because the principle is that what has fallen does not return (al-saqit la ya'ud), and the second 'iddah will not become obligatory because the divorce after the second marriage occurred before consummation, and due to divorce before consummation, no 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman. The response to Imam Zufar's proof has already passed; please see it.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
Passage type: Intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the 'iddah of a woman whose husband purchases her as a slave. The author first explains the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: When a man buys his own wife who is a slave, the marriage becomes fasid (corrupt) immediately. Since she is now his property, a slave woman upon dissolution of marriage observes 'iddah of two menstrual periods. However, while she remains his property, the 'iddah is not observed outwardly because the right of ownership prevents it. But if he then frees her, the impediment is removed, and she must observe two hayd for the fasid marriage (with mourning) and one additional hayd for manumission (without mourning). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They argue that the woman is still considered under the first marriage's possession because she remains in her husband's custody and the first 'iddah period has not elapsed. When the husband renews the marriage during that period, the possession from the first marriage substitutes for the required possession of the second marriage. Therefore, divorce after this second marriage is considered post-consummation, requiring full mahr and a new 'iddah. Imam Zufar offers a third view: The first 'iddah falls away with the second marriage (since al-saqit la ya'ud), and the second marriage ends before consummation, so no 'iddah at all. The text notes that the response to Imam Zufar has been given earlier. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the detailed reasoning of the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa indicates the dispute remains unresolved in this passage.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after dissolution of marriage before remarrying.
ملک یمین (milk yamin): Ownership by right hand; the legal impediment to 'iddah because the woman is the man's property.
حیض (hayd): Menstrual period; used as a unit for the duration of 'iddah for slave women and fasid marriages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many hayd of 'iddah are required for the slave-wife after she is freed by her husband who had previously purchased her (according to Imam Abu Hanifa)?
A) Three hayds with mourning in all
B) Two hayds with mourning and one without
C) One hayd with mourning
D) Three hayds with mourning in the first two but not the third

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah of a woman purchased by her husband involves multiple considerations: the corrupt marriage, ownership, and manumission; scholars differ on whether a second marriage is recognized.

Iddah for Dhimmi and Harbi Women: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding 'iddah for a dhimmi woman and a harbiyah emigrant, and explain the evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
No 'iddah for dhimmi and harbi women unless pregnant, per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn require 'iddah by analogy.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The issue concerns whether a dhimmi woman divorced by her dhimmi husband must observe 'iddah, and whether a harbiyah woman who becomes Muslim and emigrates to Dar al-Islam must observe 'iddah. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of Quranic evidence and the nature of rights (huquq al-adami) in 'iddah. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyse how Hanafi scholars derive rulings from primary texts and apply legal maxims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two separate cases: (1) a dhimmi man divorces his dhimmi wife; (2) a harbiyah woman (from dar al-harb) becomes Muslim and emigrates to dar al-Islam. In both cases, the question is whether 'iddah is obligatory.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in both scenarios, no 'iddah is required unless the woman is pregnant. If not pregnant, she may remarry immediately.
The pregnancy exception protects lineage (nasab).
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that 'iddah is obligatory in both cases, regardless of pregnancy status, because separation by emigration is analogous to separation by divorce or death.
They use qiyas (analogical reasoning).
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's evidence
Abu Hanifa cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahinah 60:10): 'There is no sin upon you if you marry them' – the permission implies no obligation of 'iddah. Additionally, 'iddah involves a human right (haqq al-adami), which is not applicable to a harbi woman who is like inanimate matter (jammad). For dhimmi, his opinion is conditioned on their community not believing in 'iddah.
The dalala of the verse is zanni (not explicit about 'iddah), but the absence of mention supports his view.
5
Analyse the Sahibayn's evidence
The Sahibayn argue by qiyas: if separation occurred by divorce or death, 'iddah is obligatory; similarly, separation by tabayun al-darayn (change of abode) should also require 'iddah. They do not distinguish between a harbi and any other woman regarding human rights.
Their analogy is based on the legal cause (illa) of marital dissolution.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'the first opinion is more correct' (al-awwal asahh), indicating that Abu Hanifa's position is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
This tarjih is from the author of Al-Hidayah.

نات العدة
اختیار میں لائے ہیں کتاب النکاح میں، اور ابو حنیفہ کا قول اس صورت میں ہے کہ جب ذمیوں کا اعتقاد یہ ہو کہ ذمیہ مطلقہ پر عدت نہیں ہے۔ اور رہی مہاجرہ ( یعنی جو مسلمان ہو کر دار الاسلام کی طرف ہجرت کر آئی ) تو اس کے بارے میں صاحبین کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جدائی اگر کسی دوسرے سبب سے واقع ہوتی تو عدت واجب ہوتی۔ اسی طرح دار الکفر چھوڑ کر دار الاسلام میں چلے آنے سے جو جدائی واقع ہوئی اس میں بھی عدت واجب ہوگی ) برخلاف اس کے جب مرد نے ہجرت کی اور عورت کو ( دار الحرب ) میں چھوڑا ( تو اس پر عدت نہیں ) کیونکہ اس کو حکم شرع نہیں پہنچا ہے۔
اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا لا جناح علیک ان تنكحوهن یعنی تم پر گناہ نہیں ہے کہ ان سے نکاح کرو۔ اور اس لئے کہ جہاں عدت واجب ہوتی ہے اس میں آدمی کا حق ہوتا ہے اور حربی جہاد کے ساتھ ملحق ہے حتی کہ وہ ملکیت کا محل ہوسکتا ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ حاملہ ہو کیونکہ اس کے پیٹ میں ثابت النسب بچہ ہے اور ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اس حاملہ سے نکاح جائز ہے اور اس سے وطی نہ کرے، جیسے حاملہ من الزنا اور قول اول اصبح ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں دو صورتیں مذکور ہیں ایک یہ کہ ذمی مرد نے اپنی زمیہ بیوی کو طلاق دی دوم یہ کہ حر بسید عورت مسلمان ہو کر دار الکفر یا دار الاسلام کی طرف نکل آئی ، تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر یہ عورت نکاح کرلے تو شرعاً درست ہے لیکن اگر یہ عورت حاملہ ہو تو نکاح جائز نہیں ہو گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں عورت پرعدت واجب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ زمیہ عورت پر عدت کے وجوب اور عدم وجوب میں امام صاحب اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ایسا ہے جیسا کہ نکاح محارم میں تھا اور یہ اختلاف بالدلائل باب نکاح اہل الشرک میں گذر چکا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ امام صاحب کا قول اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ اہل ذمہ کا اعتقاد یہ ہو کہ ذمیہ مطلقہ پر عدت نہیں ہوتی۔
اور رہی وہ عورت جو دار الحرب سے ہجرت کر کے دارالاسلام میں آگئی تو اس کے بارے میں صاحبین کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر دار الاسلام میں تبائین دارین کے علاوہ اور کسی سبب سے فرقت واقع ہوئی مثلا طلاق کی وجہ سے یا موت کی وجہ سے تو بالا تفاق عدت واجب ہوتی پس ایسے ہی جب تبایین دارین یعنی عورت کے دار الاسلام میں آنے سے فرقت واقع ہوئی تو بھی عدت واجب ہوگی۔ البتہ اگر مرد کے دار الحرب سے ہجرت کر کے دارالاسلام میں آگیا اس کی بیوی دار الحرب میں مقیم رہی تو اس صورت میں عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہو گی کیونکہ دارالحرب میں اس کو شریعت کا حکم نہیں پہنچا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے، لا جناح علیکم ان تنكحوهن پوری آیت اس طرح ہے يا ايها الذين أمنوا اذا جاء كم المؤمنات مهاجرات فامتحنوهن الله اعلم بايمانهن فان علمتموهن مؤمنات فلا ترجعو هن الى الكفار لا هن حل لهم ولا هم يحلون لهن و اتو هم ما انفقوا و لا جناح عليكم ان تنكحوهن اذا اتيتموهن أجورهن الآية (سوره ممتحنه) اے ایمان والو! جب تمہارے پاس مسلمان عورتیں ( دار الحرب سے ) ہجرت کر کے آئیں تو تم ان کا امتحان کر لیا کرو
And if a dhimmi divorces a dhimmi woman, there is no 'iddah upon her. Similarly, if a harbiyah (enemy woman) comes to us as a Muslim, and she marries, it is permissible unless she is pregnant. All this is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: 'Upon her and upon the dhimmi woman, 'iddah is obligatory.' As for the dhimmi woman, the difference in it is similar to the difference in their marriage to their mahrams, which we have explained in the Book of Nikah. The statement of Abu Hanifa is when their belief is that there is no 'iddah upon her. As for the emigrant woman (muhajirah), the argument of the two (Sahibayn) is that if separation occurred due to another cause, 'iddah would be obligatory, so too due to separation by emigration. Contrary to when a man emigrates and leaves her (behind in dar al-harb) due to lack of conveyance. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is the saying of Allah, may He be exalted: 'There is no sin upon you if you marry them.'... And because where 'iddah is obligatory, there is the right of human beings (haqq al-adami), and the harbi is like inanimate matter (jammad) such that he is subject to ownership, unless she is pregnant because there is a child of established lineage in her belly. And it is related from Abu Hanifa that it is permissible to marry her but not to have intercourse with her, like a pregnant woman from adultery. And the first opinion is more correct.

Translation: And if a dhimmi man divorces a dhimmi woman, there is no 'iddah upon her. Similarly, if a harbiyah woman becomes Muslim and comes to our country, there is no 'iddah upon her. So if she marries, it is permissible unless she is pregnant. All this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: 'Upon this woman and upon the dhimmi woman, 'iddah is obligatory.' In any case, regarding the dhimmi woman, the difference is similar to the difference regarding the dhimmi's marriage to their mahrams, and we have brought this in the Book of Nikah. And Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is in the case when the dhimmi's belief is that there is no 'iddah upon the divorced dhimmi woman. As for the muhajirah (who emigrates to Dar al-Islam as a Muslim), the proof of the Sahibayn is that if separation had occurred due to another cause, 'iddah would be obligatory. Similarly, with the separation caused by leaving Dar al-Kufr and coming to Dar al-Islam, 'iddah would also be obligatory. Contrary to the case when the man emigrates and leaves the woman (in Dar al-Harb), then there is no 'iddah upon her because the command of Shariah did not reach her.

And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that Allah said: 'No sin upon you to marry them.' And because where 'iddah is obligatory, there is a right of human beings. And the harbi is like an inanimate object, such that he can be the subject of ownership. Unless she is pregnant, because there is a child of established lineage in her womb. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that it is permissible to marry such a pregnant woman but not to have intercourse with her, like a pregnant woman from zina. And the first opinion is more correct. Explanation: In this passage, two scenarios are mentioned: first, a dhimmi man divorces his dhimmi wife; second, a harbiyah woman becomes Muslim and comes to Dar al-Kufr or Dar al-Islam. In both cases, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman. So if this woman marries, it is legally valid, but if she is pregnant, marriage is not permissible. The Sahibayn said that in both cases, 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the difference between Imam and the Sahibayn regarding the obligation or non-obligation of 'iddah upon the dhimmi woman is similar to what was in the marriage of mahrams, and this difference with proofs was mentioned in the chapter on marriage of polytheists. Note that Imam's opinion is when the people of dhimma believe that there is no 'iddah upon the divorced dhimmi woman.

As for the woman who emigrated from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, the proof of the Sahibayn is that if separation in Dar al-Islam had occurred due to some reason other than separation of the two abodes (tabayun al-darayn), for example, by divorce or death, then by consensus 'iddah would be obligatory. Similarly, when separation occurred due to tabayun al-darayn, i.e., the woman's coming to Dar al-Islam, 'iddah would also be obligatory. However, if the man emigrated from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam while his wife remained in Dar al-Harb, then in that case no 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman because the Shariah command did not reach her in Dar al-Harb. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that Allah said: 'No sin upon you to marry them.' The full verse is: 'O you who believe! When believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them...' (Surah al-Mumtahinah).
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
Passage type: Intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the 'iddah of a dhimmi woman divorced by her dhimmi husband and a harbiyah woman who becomes Muslim and emigrates. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in both cases, no 'iddah is required unless the woman is pregnant. His evidence includes the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahinah, 60:10) which permits marrying emigrant believing women without mentioning 'iddah, and the principle that 'iddah involves rights of human beings (haqq al-adami) which is not a concern for harbi women since they are like inanimate objects. However, if pregnant, 'iddah is necessary to preserve lineage. The Sahibayn argue by analogy: if separation occurs by divorce or death, 'iddah is obligatory; similarly, separation by emigration should also require 'iddah. They also consider the harbi woman like any woman, so 'iddah is due. The text notes that Abu Hanifa's ruling applies when the dhimmi community does not recognize 'iddah. The relied-upon position is stated to be the first (Abu Hanifa's) as more correct (al-awwal asahh).

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from a territory at war with Islam.
تبایین دارین (tabayun al-darayn): Separation of abodes (Dar al-Islam vs Dar al-Harb) that dissolves marital ties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is a harbiyah woman who becomes Muslim and emigrates to Dar al-Islam required to observe 'iddah?
A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if she is pregnant
D) Only if her husband also emigrates

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that 'iddah is not required for dhimmi women (if their community does not observe it) or for harbiyah emigrants unless pregnant, based on the Quranic permission and the principle that such women lack the human right in 'iddah.
